O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, very cherished sons, I have completed this book which is the conclusion of the science of medicine, and filled it with its contents, and I have finished it by its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is extinguished from all to all, so it has perished the science and has been lost, and nothing remains but the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and the futility, and the minds are closed and the knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive it together with the order of this treatment according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of cauterizing irons, and other tools of the work with the addition of declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Because for the reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is lengthened.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters into this to surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of them, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of joints, and the movement of the veins moving and resting, and the source of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because Hippocrates says that the non-skilled is not much, and with work is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that those who are not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, if they attempt to perform it, may make mistakes and harm people; thus I have often seen many times from those who engage in this science and abandon their own knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish woman who lanced an abscess of scrofula from the neck of a woman, and lanced the arteries of the neck; because so much blood issued out that the woman died between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And another mirror that treats a stone from a man of age, and the stone was large; it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for the extraction, and saw the position of the misalignment and the size of the stone, and it was clear that if they cut it, it would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And another mirror that took care of the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the breaker had a wound; and the mirror, due to lack of knowledge, placed the fracture over the wound with stitches for a long time, and did not let the wound drain, and thus it ended in such a way that the leg was completely infected and the foot and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to dislocate the leg; and when I saw it dislocated, it was in the field and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the ways of the corruption were already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another method that would crush the abscess and make it worse, and then it would inflame due to the evil of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For an abscess, when it is free of melancholic humor, it only needs that one touch with iron if it is not in a place where one can completely remove everything that is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is, where he is in danger in many positions; and I will show in each chapter of this book where he has fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, you should keep him safe so that the foolish cannot speak evil of you if you take up your arms in battle and undertake your wounds firmly and use the best way so that by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be healed; and let not the spreading diseases of great sickness overcome you; and remove your arms from what causes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiens says in some of his warnings: 'Do not take care of a seriously ill person unless you are called a fool.'
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatment into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medical cauteries of the foot, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet; and the forms of instruments, and the irons of cauteries, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and wounds, and extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; it is ordered by the main joints from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we recall the work, it is necessary that I mention the quality of aid and the new harm from each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest and most subtle science and secret knowledge; and because of this, many wise people spoke about it and agreed on it; and I do not lengthen my words much, because I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cauterization helps universally in every condition where there is matter, because the conditions are: it is to know whether the condition is hot with matter, and dry without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry weather, they divided into two groups and said that the fire cauterization is a great help; the others said the opposite: that the fire cauterization is only helpful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite claimed that cauterization helps greatly with hot and dry diseases that come from people's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and its moisture to the hot fire, you heat the body.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And no one should interfere with it except those who have experienced it, and know the chapter on cauteries from long use, and the variety of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the remedies and the space of time; for other constitutions we have little fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the symptoms gathered and agreed to the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of cures, and has greater goodness than cauterization with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fever is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members unless it has a name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by separating, and bring diseases of the malady to the member; and by chance it finds the evil The fever for its highness and for the goodness of its substance does not cause harm, if there is no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it has been above the truth of things; and for this I excuse the length of speech, because it does not please me to give you the secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they should be made in what degree the cautery should be done, and ask for permission.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is beneficial in all cases, because the harm that comes from it is quickly removed by the help of the cautery; and moreover, if the cautery is for necessary pain, not just any pain that cannot wait until the time when greater malice does not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, my son, as the foolish ones do; for the disease that is cured by the cautery has no return; and they say it thus, but it is not so, because cautery is only medicine that moves the complexion, and dries the humors that are cause of the pain, and is worth any other medicine for its quickness of its value, and for the virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the only thing that is possible is that the disease comes at any time according to the humor of the body and the nature of the disease and its virtue; and there are assembled in it the superfluities by the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless you administer cauteries in the place where there is a lack of superfluity and moisture, as cauteries of dense for the pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return much; but this has little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and it is seen; but they do not believe that cauteries work after medicine, but rather their intentions are false, and cauteries are called the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth it.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is necessary to carefully use cautery as a last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of those who are misguided.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that a cauterizing instrument of gold is better than one of iron, and they only said further that because of the quality of gold and the purity of its substance; and they said that the wounds of cautery do not fester, but I have found that this is not true, and I have seen it in some people; and a cauterizing instrument of gold is better than one of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And when you heat an instrument of gold, you should not be deceived by its color, and it has cooled somewhat; and if it is heated too much, they put it in the fire; and thus it has enough protection.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cauterization that we have armed ourselves with for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I would order this chapter on the shoulder joints from the feet, because it is easier to find there.
dou cautere olivaire	The fire cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This fire cauterization is used for moisture and cold on the head, and it is done because of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the joint to the eyes, and to the ears, and due to many dreams and tooth pain, and throat pain, and also for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that the hairs should be removed by a soluble medicine, changing the skin three or four times, according to the virtues and age and custom of the patient, which can bear it; and then repeat the treatment of the wound.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on top of his knees; after that, place the root of your palm above the root of his nail between his two eyes; and if he bleeds from the nose, heat the cauterization which is called «olivare», of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the bone signet of ink on the limb, and by descending and gradually tightening your hand little by little in restoring; then gently remove your hand, and reward the limb if you see the bone small; and if you do not see the bone, if you restart the cauterization until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take a little rope, and put it in warm and soft cotton inside, and place on the limb, and let it stay for three hours; afterwards put a moist cloth on burning; and leave it until the burn is healed; afterwards treat the wound of the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason, it helps to close it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should burn the cauterizer so much that a part of the bone is burned away, and then remove what has been burned off from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others said that one should burn the cauterizer so much above, and push it as hard as one can remove a piece of bone as wide as the needle that women put in their clothes for the reason that the humors are driven out moist; and one should keep the wound open long; afterward, one must treat and bandage it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good for all, except in some people where there is a view of fear; and I think that I should leave it; because the affected person is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and even when the affected person is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salve and mild for me, and of this use I operate in the following manner.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the main
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the main pain comes chronic and lasts a long time, one should use the remedies of years and pills called "cochie", and cleansing of head and eyes and plasters; and if one does the cauterization that we have previously mentioned, and it is not good.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care when dealing with the sick patient, as they are of a sensitive nature, and do not make it too cold; then cauterize with that fire cautery which we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying the cautery to each of the horns of the head up to the bone, as we have mentioned before, and applying the cautery called "vasselz"; and in the vessels where you put suctions; lift your hand so that you do not see too close to the bone: the hairs cause much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the cautery of the horns be more subtle than that with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head sudden pain comes, and the disease extends to the eye, and the patient is purged by medicines that are modified, and the other cures that I have mentioned in the division of diseases do not help: then you must cauterize according to two methods, namely with a medicine or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with medicine is such that you press a cloth on the painful spot and remove the scab and wrap it in a small piece of linen, and then place it on the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can replace the cloth outside the skin; and when it is replaced, hold it and keep it in place for 12 hours; then remove it and treat further with a cloth soaked in oil, and leave the wound for two or three days; then put on a cotton pad soaked in butter until the pain subsides.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the application of ointment until they are healed; and if you see that it is from some burning medicines that I have written or prescribe treatment for burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a cloak or it has a small beak, and in the middle has a small appearance; and place it on the painful limb, and hold your hand and gently stir the fire until half of the skin is burned; and remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is above, and there is abundant bleeding.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After applying gauze on a thread and placing it on the limb for three days; then apply moistened cotton with butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the cauterizing iron called "cultellare", do so at the tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this wound which is very ancient.
de emigraine	of the wound
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat the wound as we have previously mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterizing iron before mentioned of medicine and of iron does not suffice to heal it, then it is necessary to extinguish the cauterizing iron called "cultellare" until it is white; and afterwards place it on the limb at a distance of half a finger's breadth from the bone, and take your hand once, and avoid covering the artery and that it does not come near the bone; and be careful of the mandible which moves when you turn, and the nerves have no regard but the moved and that spasm does not cause pain, and be careful of the bleeding of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting it has great fear and immediately to that which is not known, and which is not studied and experienced; and leave the work in one way; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding of blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is found in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you see that this fire cautery is not sufficient for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the wound as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or from the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two knives; and this fire cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and medicines have been administered and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "poins", of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After sharpening all around the ear, where the pain is felt in both places, and separate it a little from the root of the ear because you have identified the bone of the cheek; and apply X pounds around each ear; after healing the bone as long as it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated by cauterization is no more than those that move from the mouth, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply cauterization to similar ones that come from scarring and spasm of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this appearance of torture that moves from the stream of water and cleansing of the head and throat, and does not heal, then it is necessary to cauterize the pain with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a little further from the temple, and the third in the corner of the mouth; and put the cautery in the part that opens healthily, and make the cauterization above a little bit away from the horn of the ear, and another in the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cautery so high that half of the face is burned; and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the cauterization of the knife that we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and it is necessary that the knives be a bit larger; after curing the wound as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the pain does not have fever, then make four cauterizations: two above the two horns of the head, and one on the forehead, and one on the back of the neck which is called «vasselz» as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	of laziness
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is recommended to give the patient large and modified head pills; after rubbing the entire head, place the sinapi plaster on the occipital bone, as written in the book of treatments; and this is the method of the fire cautery: if you do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is thus healed, good; if not, make three cauteries on the head by descending from the neck to the collarbone, and leave a space of one inch between each cautery; and the treatment is as for the others, and if you have seen them put them back, and if the pains are severe, make one cautery in the middle; and if it is misaligned, make two more on the two horns, and treat as before mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold from the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to clean the head with wool and the things we have previously mentioned; after that, remove the evil from the head, then make a cautery on the head and under each horn, and behind and three times above the spine of the neck; and if you have more trouble, and the body is moist and the pain is severe, and the disease is outside, then make four cauteries above the spine of the back; and leave it until the worst is over, and withdraw your hand; afterwards, cure it as long as it is healthy, and let the cauteries that are called "olivare" be as we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use cauterization except for those that are bleeding, and it is first necessary to modify the brain of years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the pain is great and suffering from lack of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot bear the suffering, give them gargarisms and mastication modifying the brain often with good meat; then relieve the head in the middle, and perform cauterization according to what we have said before, and cauterize above the vessel, and above each horn; and if the pain is far and suffering, perform cauterization as I have said to those who have paralysis and softening of the body, above the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterization be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the pain is intense, apply the subtle cauterization in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture is great, then use the cautery of parts as we have said for those who are paralyzed.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy, the excess declining towards melancholy is wet, then give it to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After relieving the head of pain; then apply a well-made tortilla, like a circle, and put it on the head; and if the pains increase, and are held firmly from all sides; then present the liniment, and it should be mixed with fresh butter of elder; and heat it gently in the fire, so that the patient can bear it; afterwards empty the circle from inside towards the head, and let it cool; and do this to the head every week once with another good regimen until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you have seen cauterization done by making several pricks with the whole cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the brain and increases it; then put on gauze soaked in butter and green goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the first sign comes to the eyes as I have indicated in the previous section, then begin and give the patient to drink a medicine mundifying the head, and keep it from all moisture, and make it sweat or bathe it several times a day on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Then command the patient to turn his head, and cauterize behind the head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples at the same time, or one if it is only one; and cover all the cautery with the veins and arteries that are outside the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and keep from bleeding of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with a cloth as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	I will teach you how to extract arteries and make incisions with caution, as you would do; and never burn or heat anything outside of the two lower bones.
dou cors des larmes	The path of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed to be above the veins or on the sides of the arteries that are in the appearance of the main deformed; and one sees that it is superfluous cold phlegm, then use the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning of this work: burn the forehead, and two burn above the temples, and two burn outside the two lower bones; and if there is more, then burn wisely with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give a drink of bad herbs three times; after that, apply the chief remedy, and perform cauterization or middle cauterization with olive oil; and make two cauterizations with the "clavilis" above the two sorci, a little outside the ears; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this cauterization which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	For what purpose this form is used.
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you have made two cauterizations on the two sorcilz as long as they are; and do not leave the hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that does not hold the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has ever been when the hairs of the oil are converted to the parchedens, and they hold the oil, and it is made cauterization according to two manners: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient under the paper of the hairs; after, sign above the hairs a figure that is as similar to the shape of the mustache, and be the beginning of the sign below the hairs; then put cotton moistened in oil and musk mallow on the oil, then heat the cauterizer in this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the figure that you have marked a little and not too many times, where the curer is in the right place; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retreating, and the hairs raised to the point of oil; then gently touch it, and leave it like this for three hours, then put cotton moistened in butter on the burn until the blister is opened; after the healing of the wound as long as it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come back, and the paper is softened, then start the cauterizing again on the same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level, and is even, and does not prick at the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fire cautery is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then take parchment in the shape of a leaf of mint; then take French soap and live chalk, each one, and grind them together well; and apply it vigorously, so that it does not cool, then spread it over the form you have made like the leaf of mint, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the disease remains only in one eye, it should be opened in one, and similarly; and put some cotton moistened with oil behind the ear; and the patient should be in a sound mind and put his hand on the medicine, and press the pouch and move it every time the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, because it feels stinging like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then you will have the knowledge of the remedy to your task.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the burning has passed, if the limb is raised from the fire, and if it rises as it was raised by constraint of fire or by incision, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then still apply the remedy to the limb or the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are set; then put cotton moistened in water on it as much as the pains are chosen, after care the limb of the burn which is called «dyafenis» and others, until they are healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have the task to stay within your work, be careful not to cut into the medicine with those.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs are pricked in the oil, then restart the medicine above the one that is softened by the proper paper, as you did before; then cure it until it is healed; and this is the form of the fuller's earth:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And it is known that the sizes of men are different in size and smallness, and according to what your constraints are; and do not reply with the wrong way to him who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistulas by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not work, then it is necessary to cauterize them in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put his head on your clean; and wipe the sweat from his forehead between your hands in this manner that it does not move, nor remove his head; afterwards put cotton moistened with urine or vinegar on the oil; afterwards heat the cauterizer which is ready: and it is fastened to the head like the form of a pen of feathers, together with the other end of the cauterizer; if you see, it is appointed from one head to the other, and if you see, it is also like a tent; but anyway, this which is fastened is good for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it is opened, and the pus is removed, and dried; and if it is closed, open it again, and remove the flesh from outside the boil; afterwards, put the cautery hot and well, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the neck above the oil, so that your hand does not do harm; and put the cautery in the grease of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just at the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, if you have experience, and start the cautery again once more, and leave it for three days; afterwards, put moistened cotton in butter, and use a drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then put on corrosive medicine until the bone is revealed; and the king according to what he would have in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that no ancient people mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	To the fistula, and feel the leg; after put in the wound a subtle powder of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make of the quantity of a grain; and hold your hand firmly, and do not move the hairs until the powder melts into its oil; and it is necessary to put above the hair on the wound moist cotton wool near or far: the powder heals the leg of the fistula, and brings great health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you must administer poultices to the wound, and bring the fistula back to the core of the wound according to what is proper for that limb.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are cracks in the lips that are called "hair", and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing needle according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the patient in those crevices until he comes just before dawn; then, after care, the broken bone is set as soon as it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the groin
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the groin or bladder, or palate, or at the roots of teeth, after it has fermented and rotted and aged and become a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, but it does not improve: therefore it is necessary that you use cauterization according to the size of the fistula; then plug or puncture the fistula, and keep your hand there until the iron has reached the end of the bone, and behind the bone; and do this once or twice, after caring for what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, if necessary, discover the bone and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines but it does not work, then put the tip of a hot iron in your healthy mouth; afterwards, apply the cauterizer in the shape of a needle on the tooth; and place the cauterizer deeply into the tooth, holding your hand steady until the pain reaches the root of the tooth; then release your hand and continue the cauterization as you wish; afterwards, fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let them chew some willow leaves for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the tooth that was moving is now fixed, and the gum is softened by being held, and the moisture is corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or wetness, and medical remedies do not work, then it is necessary to use cauterization in two ways: with butter cauterization and fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cauterization is such that you take butter from a fresh cow, and the end in an iron or tin spoon; then take cotton and wrap it over the point of a tent, and dip it into hot butter, and put it on the painful tooth firmly and hold until it is cooled; and so do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that dipped wool and cotton in hot butter, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron as far as the heat of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Use a hot iron to cauterize as it is such that you grasp a needle of iron or brass, and it is large enough that the heat does not reach the mouth of the wound; after heating the cautery, because of which the form will come out afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be gone the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the wound fill its mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cauterization, and then to press it; and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform cauterization with the type of fire you wish, and according to what you have available; and it is in the form of a cane:
des scrophules	of splinters
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the splinters are watery and cold, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cauterizing iron with the following form, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the other side; and place the cauterizing iron hot above the abscess once, or as often as necessary until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, then apply the cauterizing iron according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and place wet cotton moistened in butter on the wound until the burn is healed; afterwards treat with eye drops and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the uterus:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary to first evacuate the hairs by medicines soluble; afterwards apply cauterization to the root of the neck, and be careful not to bring the heat too close to the throat, but with a small amount.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards apply another cauterization to the joint of the collarbone and the top of the spine, and let the cauteries that are called "clavicle" because of the form we have mentioned; and cure the limb as we have said until it is healed.
de la toust	of the whole
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of pormon are of cold moisture, and the maladies have no fever or sweat, and is the ancient disease, then make two cauterizations on the forehead in their sight; and the other cauterization goes between the breasts; and let the cauterizations be called "clavile" according to the form that is mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cauterization by holding the entire cauterization that is called "poins" because of the form it has in the disease of the ears; and let the poins be just a few, or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, the patient according to what has been said before, and let it be that the cauteries are applied at three intervals according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter, because you make three of them in a cup.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, shave the hairs on their back and on their ribs; afterwards, relieve the pain in the armpit with your right hand; and if the joint is misaligned inside, then heat the cauteries that have two nails at this point in this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the wound as long as it does not perforate from the side, and bring the four cautery together; and for this reason, cauterization is made with the cautery that has three needles, because the shape of cauterization is these four needles; and they are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three needles.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never are they placed on this one nerve because it has eight cautery.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cautery on the broken bones with silk; after resting the pain, and do not move the member by long tension until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, this thing happens quickly, then make a cauterization above the thick part of the cauterizing knife, or with many cauterizations in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and it is covered by moisture and is healthy of the pain.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come cold and much moisture until it is at its condition, and are multiplied by vomiting to him, and are customary ways of cures and he does not improve, then it is necessary that the pain be soothed above his back, and extends his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, make three cauteries with the sharp spoon, one after the other, as much as the quantity of a drop, at all the cautery clavicle, and two cauteries afterwards on the two ribs until the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and have equal space between them so that they do not touch each other when they grow together; and let the cauteries be so sharp that they do not press the two parts of the chest together, and let the figure of the cauteries be in this form without jostling:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that the cauteries are too large in the stomach according to this form, and the one who is afraid of this cauterie, cauterizes by pinching and holding above the stomach, i. point according to the quantity that you see in the enche; then cauterize all the cautery which is called «poins».
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the cure that we have had before, as long as they are healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver causes pain from heat and moisture and excessive windiness, as long as it is not removed from its natural condition by excess; and the pains are relieved according to what we have said in divisions, and it does not help much, it is necessary that the pains be soothed above its hypochondriac region, where the ears of the stomach come; and there should be three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity above the liver, below the hypochondria, where the ears of the stomach come; and there should be a space between each cautery the thickness of one finger; and let the cautery be long like the body, and do not press much with your hand all over the cautery; and let it be applied only to the half of the belly, and let the pains be stretched above its feet; and if it cannot, then let it be lying down, and extend its legs, and raise its arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to cauterize these cuts with a cauterizing iron, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and you guard that you do not burn all the flesh, for you would make it harder all over the body; and that it does not come near boiling, for the flesh is very delicate there, and the skilled ones to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess in the liver, and you see if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the web: if it is in the flesh, he feels the pain not too strong; and if it is in the web, he feels sharp pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment is done, it is necessary that the hairs be singed over the head; then wipe the area where the abscess was, and then heat the cautery which is similar to the iron, of which there is a form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cautery until the wound is closed, and comes just to the skin, until the pus is all out; then treat according to the treatment of wounds as long as they are healed; and it is not necessary that this cautery be used except by those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have never been corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, it can be bravely overcome, and in all ways, it seems to me that it is worth leaving it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cautery of the chest
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should apply the cauterizing of the chest with the roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and dry it, and also as thick and long as your finger; and moisten it in oil, and take the cautery to the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the shoulder and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the spine, declining a little behind; and one cautery in the least, and the other above the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest, and one in front of the cautery between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make an opening as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And the ancients said that no man uses fire cautery similar to a razor, and they scrape it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess; and when it comes to the abscess, it is as painful as we have said about the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the wounds are fatal now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
