Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the ancient "wound healer," and you should apply pressure to the painful area that has this disease, whether it is on the front or back; then make three incisions evenly along the length of the front; and one of the incisions as two just above the jaw, and the others two at the sides of the ribs, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are at the sides of the ribs; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the lower jaws, and apply a quantity of three doses across each wound; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth to soak up the blood, then plug the opening with the following form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made from the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the matter that is between the two cuts from the eye socket to the top of the bone, then make another incision from the other side of the same second incision, and then extract this sponge.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert the instrument called "curette" into the first cut, it is very sharp on one side and dull on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side of the curette towards the eye and the dull side towards the bone, and continue scraping until it reaches the same cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the eyes until the incision is continued up to where it opens, and then make another incision in the same place towards the other side; and then extract the blood equally, and express the wound for the blood taken; then put a piece of old cotton in each incision, and put on dressings of milled cloth soaked in wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure that abscesses do not come; and the next day remove the bandage, and apply a great amount of boiled honey, then the cure of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures as necessary until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	renewing of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes for cautery with a usual custom, and you see the eyes tight and small, and weakened vision, and burnt papers; and the hairs are shaved, and where the shaving is done, there is great pain, and the limbs are numb; therefore, these accidents and that cautery come only from many incisions, and the patient's cure that is, if this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a deep cut into the forehead, and another one wide at the forehead.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins from the cut on the right temple to the left temple, and let the incision be just to the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that vibrate at the gum; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood onto a sponge, then clean between the two lips of the cut and put in old cotton, and wrap with linen; then bind above with moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to form, then care for things that are excreted, which are like char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of clay, and make a poultice; and administer this in these wounds to apply charper for all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the deafness of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which chiefs in the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or stones, or pebbles of sand or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas; or things flowing like water and vinegar and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it chiefs in the ear pebble or other kind of thing that does not fit well in the ear, does not grow in the ear, then put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see an arrow, if any drops of blue oil or fennel oil distill, then apply extraction; and the effect is to make him spit out the condition, and stop his nose when he sneezes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around his ear; and elevate the ear.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, then apply extraction with fine needles, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by the needles, it is good; if not, then apply extraction with a fine siphon of small doubled-up cloth; and if it does not come out by this, then take a needle and blow the head of the needle or the hole of the ear very hard with candle wax so that nothing can enter with the needle; then pull it out properly, for many times it comes out like we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take some glue and put it on the ears, and put any instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the glue above the arrow or whatever, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not do all of these things that we have said, then you must quickly lance the ear as soon as an abscess forms and blood comes out, and spasm; and the manner of the lancing is that you first cleanse the pain from the head, and extract the pus according to the measure of its power, then place the pain between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small lance in the root of the ear at the fat or flesh where it hangs; and let the lancing be as a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it vigorously to your mouth; and the cure until they are healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is small and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the following subtle form of spatula:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that small one.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make it too narrow when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine forceps and au succier, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the acute case when it is in the ear, it is necessary that the hairs use blowing of a soft condition first, and widen the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie across the very ear itself where the sharp is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of the sky, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not the sky, take many thin pieces according to the length of your finger and lightly heat them in the fire; and put the bad ones or a piece of ear, and go up from its other foot, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop making the stone against stone until the sharp is all out, and thus it jumps all out; and if you see, take the reed, and boil one of the pieces in the ear, and the other piece hold from fire until the thinnest reed is burned; then make others as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a mouse and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, where one can feel it, then use instruments for extraction; and it is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the division and if they do not improve, then it is necessary to look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with delicate forceps, and if there are none, then take a needle of this type.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tight below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And push the most subtle head into the ear according to the amount of pain, then it should be applied to the whole chain; do this often until all the worms are seen.

Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or lead is made into small holes, and above over the pot to distill; and to press during the distillation with a well-made silver instrument for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you see from your medicines in the cane, and the cane should be in the ear; then boil within the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or the smell of the ear; and the bad taste is inside, and the distillation is a small amount poured into the fire as well as when it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear deafness
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some sort of ear wax; and the same thing happens to men by deafness from an injury, or a bone growing inside the ear, and this deafness never comes from within the ear, if one cannot see it; and it always comes from outside the ear, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from within, if one cannot see it, is a severe infection in many positions, and in this case, where one sees it, it is necessary to put the ear with the bad side towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening of the eardrum, if the work has all that space of which is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the burning be applied all around and behind the ear, so it does not burn the ear; if the wart is made of charred hair or the skin of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and the copper lightly, until that char is completely burned off.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wart is inside the ear, then take a fine razor and slightly warm it at the fire, then put it on the skin of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the wart that causes the patient to have a greasy feeling in the ear, slightly pierce it, and make sure not to hurt the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian oil.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not move the wound until it is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rosewater, and powder it with vitriol; and if you see inflammation in the ear, it is recommended that you remove the tent and apply another tent made of rosewater and wax, as long as the inflammation is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is a flow of blood, soak an sponge and wipe it with cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the flow of blood which are to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the charred papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method for preparing paper from the bark of trees when they are wet and then dry, so it is necessary to stretch them with nails and pliers, and the root of a glass bottle from its roots; then put it on the lead-glass broken.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decortication, then cauterize with a subtle lens-like cauterizer, and the cauterizer after the incision is good for muses; and often they repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	often come in papers certain things that seem like gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail", and is an assembly of moisture large in the paper above and below; the works are such: take care if the hail moves from one part to another, and it is a simple thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take pictures, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you do not cover it with a slight perforation in the paper, it does not hurt the patient; and if the fracture is large, it gathers at one seam, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, because the inflammations restore it quickly and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the large splinter is falling downwards into the depths of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the splinter on some tweezers, and hold it with a cloth and press from one side and the other; and if the paper is moved by the incision, it does not hurt anything; and when the splinter is cut, pour some water with strong salt, and cure the limb of which it has entered until the wounds are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is rubbed into the paper above, and it has more in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears gather in their eyes; and because they lie down they lean on their faces, and sleep on them, and their papers are outside their eyelids moist with which the exinach swells and covers them.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb to your ears and feel the cracking sound between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of the work is such that the hairs put their head in your ear; then take a cloth of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount that contains cracking sound from each part, then place it over it; and press with both ears on one side and the other, so that the cracking sound is assembled within the circle; then cut into the middle of the moisture at the spatula, making a cut of large width, and not larger than the wound made on the vein; and cut the skin until you come to the cracking sound; and in many positions of the cracking sound, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take the cloth from all over the room and fold it between your hands, turning your hand to the right and left until it is evenly spread; and do not press into the wound, that you do not come to the entire space of the oil, that you do not harm it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not open at the beginning of the wound, slightly scratch the wound until it opens; then spread the cloth as we have said, then wipe the drapes in a soft and sharp manner, and place them on the limb, and spread them evenly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who breathe and place on to corrupt the moisture that is remaining.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, let the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the healer comes to the abscess, let them apply wet dressings until they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hairs, and are awake, if they harm the eyes, and bring on diseases as tears accustomed and softening of papers and whitening, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in four ways: either by cauterization together with fire, or by medicine, according to what is before or the chapter of cauterization, and is done either by incision and stitching, or by lances, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the wound in your hand, then return the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a needle at the end of all the thread; and let it be on the side of the paper or where the hairs grow beyond these hairs, and draw the thread above the edge of the paper, and return the scissors to the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs adjusted, covering all the surface from the great arm to the small; then draw the thread, and place on the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then above the paper a figure of a bandage, like the belly of a goose, and throughout it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you saw lifted the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If there is a person who has skill in coping with great quantities of paper according to how the paper is molded; then make all the space above the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large leg down to the small one; and let the first wound be near the hairs at the base of the root, then close the opening in one of the two angles of the needle, then scrape off the skin; then bring together the two lips at a seam of an needle with all the thread of fine silk, and squeeze out the blood, and make the superfluous hairs above the two edges to any things glued, if you see that it is made thus; and if not, if you do not have care for it, then leave the seam and the threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without sewn things, which are drying and constricting, because the paper revives at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is withered (as they say of the ancients), and it is work without fear; and if there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper in a shape which is as equal to the shape of the mirror, if you have told, at three points according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then copper which surmounts as small equal forces according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or it has a thread, and put the figure in the bobbin; and the other thread over the big arm, and the second thread over the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have signed, as we have told you, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and never once have that the hair of the paper is converted: if you must use what we have said of the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of dogs is as follows: first, you convert the paper and the thread according to what I have said, then make two dogs by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and its width; and hold the two ends in the parts where you hold the threads; then bring them together subtly above the paper of the oil, and keep the two dogs from the two parts form; and leave it thus for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and rot and putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, if the thread is strong, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound has been covered with the paper, and the hairs will not grow back; and this is the form of the two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and in this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a thin needle, and the silk thread soft and thin; then assemble the hairs and pull out one and the other thinly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly in the hunt, and pull the hairs of the other thread; then put the hairs on your skin so that the work is not revealed, for it is a thin and delicate work, then push the needle through the entire hunt at the base of the hair raised, and let it pierce the paper gently until you remove it from the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the hunt, and let that hair in the hunt, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand until the hairs come out all over the hunt with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the hunt is treated and the hair does not come with it, then treat the hunt according to the instructions you have given, until the hunt comes out completely and you can see it through the oil; then treat the hunt and the thread, and close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows on top; if the hair is small, accompany it with a long hair from the goats, and raise it with the other one until it is extended and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the stirring of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the purpura, comes from the oil, there are two methods: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it comes by wounding, or cutting, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of the work in it is that you break that suture, and dry the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and it is only necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but in the work of things that are softening, such as fenugreek; and rosemary and sage and linseed seeds boiled, and ointments of melted quillion poured into any of the oils, and there is wrapped a tent, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your care are that you take precaution to ensure they do not return to their previous form; and this work that we have written is only to prevent them from returning to their previous state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the ear
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental ones come from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way of this work is that you hold an awl, in which it has a double thread, and the thread in the ear, and then make it pierce from the right side to the left, so that the thread comes out of both ears; then the ear is placed above the entire awl, and the covering is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the groove, and return the paper, and make two cuts or at the angles of the incision that you have made, and make two angles so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter that has no «I Greek»; then remove that char, according to the quantity that its cost is away from, of what it is said about the paper, then add the two missing parts, and tie them with a thread of wool; then the cure of what we have said about the medicines that soften, and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or stitch or cauterization, then it is necessary to make a plain cut outside of the hairs and papers, as I have previously mentioned; then squeeze between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very different in form, and the wise masters compare all the means possible so that they can make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the work and tools in many different positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	and of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bandaging has been done by many people in a somewhat sloppy manner, where the paper above is soaked with the white of oil, and it cannot move or do its natural workings, then you must therefore bring out the point of a razor from outside the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers, until you scrape off what is hard to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too thin, so that the pain cannot suffer that the spatula is too sharp nor blinds the oil; and let your incision, from which you scrape that assembly, lightly, so that the paper regains its natural form; and that whole assembly is healed, and nothing is ever done in strong vinegar or salt water, and lift up weak sweet wine, and colic; then put between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and put over the oil moistened wool in abundance of oil; and after the dressing use weak wine and other healing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow joint of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two types of elbow joints: one is nervous and resembles a hard, thick skin, and the other is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and heated with pincers, cannot be moved; both start near the large arm and grow slowly until they cover the entire eye and light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the hairs are placed on top of your hand, then the eyelids are opened; and take the paper in your hand, then bend the elbow with pincers of small doubled-over, and place it above; then take a needle, and put the hair of a horse, or a cow, or a cow, and the thread strongly; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the eyelid, and push the entire needle through, and tie the elbow with a thread and place it above, and shave all the hair on the side of the elbow that points to the pearl and silk to the hair just below, then cut the remaining in the root of the arm at all the subtle spatula and with small forces, and leave the natural skin of the arm so that by the incision no tears flow as usual; and once it was only the eyelid that was stuck to the thread, and if so, shave all the soft tissue as follows:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be sure that the spatula does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the prunelle is not pierced; and after the incision pour a little bit of broken silk thread oil, and a poultice made of litharge, and leave it on the other side; then care for the wound as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the joint is not very nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the prunelle cannot enter, often this resemblance of a joint of medicines is cured; and it is done as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, then apply oil to the pain, and take the spatula lightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully rub the joint gently, and if you see that it does not soften and the reason is close, then sprinkle from your mouth into the oil mixture made of turpentine and red wine and beeswax, and extinguish the oil just before the other hour; then continue the other work according to this same method, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, such as an abscess, then milk it, and first cure the abscess until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is black at night due to great harm, then soak it in oil at dawn, and apply a part of it and not all at once, until tears do not come; then pour in the oil a red wine that is made from litargyr.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men never grow red flesh, and it covers the pupil and restrains above the papers and turns to a baluster rose; and the work is that the hairs put their head in your skin, then the work the hairs, and all that flesh has suitable incisions for this, and holds it by force; then cover the first flesh, and go all shaving to the razor at the end, and be careful not to bleach the oil at the work; and let the incision of the space we have said in the incision of the nail and as small forces of which we take the previous, as the shape after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is accomplished and all the flesh is removed, then use the oil of silk broken or you distill red wine and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil afterwards cotton with absinth, so that it is assured of an abscess; and if nothing remains, and the skin does not heal, and you doubt a serious abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for a serious abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make all flesh that is treated in the oil by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you alleviate the care of each weakness of the natural vein; and of the accidental vein, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	which are red veins that cover over the eye, and take away its work and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Then the work is therefore to first look at that eye, in which those veins are, and outside, and there is no other disease except that one; then direct it in this way: command the pain to put its head in your healthy place, then suspend those veins all around according to its wisdom, and let the outlines be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be done twice a degree in one course according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then apply those forces to the veins gently, and wipe away the blood an hour later, until you can remove those veins from the oil; and be careful not to pierce the oil with points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cope with those veins; and when you have done this, distill green and red colibrium into the oil to corrupt what remains from before.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all the blood in that hour, then apply a plaster on top of the oil with things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it sit for some time until the pain is eased and it is ensured that an abscess has formed, then restart according to this method as long as it is not healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror calls this "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cauterization and medicine as I have previously mentioned, and it does not heal, then you should make an incision over the abscess where it must die, and drain all the pus that is inside, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then remove all the instrument that is inside this form; it is called "hard callus", and make a new one from fair iron in its place, and sharpen it as a lime if it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the bone of the broken limb, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that corruption is removed; and do this once, then restore the bone to remedies that dry out.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is sound, and there is no pain, and the body of the wound is sound, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not infected, and no bad accidents come, then remove it when it is healed; if not, there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula to the opening of the neck according to this form: and you must remove the bone the second time by fire, and by wet remedies, and when it is removed, take the flesh according to this form, and let the wound be of iron at three angles, and let the fistula be attenuated just as you see it here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone above the arm, and keep your hand away from the oil for a while, then return to the full extent of the forearm until it pierces the bone and you feel the pain as if it were coming from its own position; and afterwards, restore the limb with dry medicines, as I have indicated, and when the char is born and hardens the limbs, if the matter goes to the elbow, it is a lighter thing for the pain.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are widely open and do not move at all, and do not become dislocated or displaced, then you must bind the pain; then clean it, then apply leeches or a blister to draw out the poison, then place it on the oil mixed with acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are soft enough, and double each one into four, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount that the eyes have in their matter; then strain it through a strong cloth, and restart the leeches or blister to draw out the poison without hurting; then remove the leeches and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the eyes become dislocated again, you must bind them tightly; if they do not improve, then restart the bandage and cloths and the oil and leeches as long as they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	For the tearing of a vein, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	For the tearing of a vein, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly inflamed, prick them with a fine needle that comes from under the oil, and draw out the moisture and wipe away the inflammation, and immediately apply this; then extract it as much as necessary until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from under the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a bowel that is assembled in the oil, resembling a sharp descent, and it is not truly sharp; and the way of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit with the sore on the chair straight and upright, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move the muff until you see the bowel coming up to your eyes; then sew it up, and do not wipe away and do not dissolve it, and see the things as they should be; and if it does not come out, although it is sharp, and if the things that are wiped away from the bowel are not straight as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you let the pain rest between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it above the corneal thread and gently by the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal thread and the crown, until the arrow is out; and when it is out, then pour hot honey mixed with melted honey, or honey or fenugreek boiled and honey, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oils of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similar oils in the division, and what is needed to pierce; if you work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the hairs between your hands crossed, outside of the light for the sun, and the clean oil pressed and held very tightly; then put the paper of the oil to your right hand if the hairs are on the left, or to your left hand if the hairs are on the right; then take in your right hand if the hairs are on the left, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if the hairs are on the right; then put the point of the instrument over the thick part of the oil on the blanchor of the arm, then press the instrument called «almagda» virtuously, and restore your hand as long as it pierces through the blanchor of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the front of the measure of the space that is from the gold to the end of the needle; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cloth, and then put the instrument above it or where the sharp is, then press out one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he is now sharp, then he sees the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a short time, and if he becomes sharp again, put the finger with the instrument, and when it is well attached and does not rise, gently twist it slightly around your hand; then place a small piece of silk on the eye and leave it inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a warm compress or wet cloth soaked in rose oil and plenty of honey, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	And those who are from our time, apply it with plenty of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are some people who have very hard eyes, then you must use the tool called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore, pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not move it too much in front, but make the eye soft, then push the hardness, as we have said; and at the completion of the work compare to the lethargy that occurs, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and avoid all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and lie according to his disposition until the next day; then release him in the same dark room, and test his sight, and see some things, and then return the thread to the seventh day; and it does not matter that you do this after the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you raise it, because the sharp pain quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should apply a poultice of warm oil before the seventh hour, and strengthen it with what satisfies the abscess; and when it is calmed, remove the bandage and place on its face a yellow ointment to cover any opening, and let it be set in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then gradually increase the amount of light, and it will return to its place; and be sure that no one should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in some countries people practice this procedure, where the sharp instrument is inserted, but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, nor have I read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of amalgams, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of pure tin properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they are the masters of this very subtlety, and the others in three angles awake.
de la char sor le neis	of the chain for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do chains or noses grow out of different wounds, because there are some that seem like scorpions with many feet; and if there are such, or if there is an enlarged chain of bad color, and if there is a chain of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those chains that are sores, and not enlarged, it is necessary to make the pain between your hands against the sun; and work its nostrils, and pour the nail polish on those chains, and remove them; because it is necessary to hold the subtle spirit of one part, as long as you know that that chain is completely gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there remains anything that cannot be removed, open it with all the subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if it is an abscess that does not heal, scrape it as it should; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize it until the wound is no longer wet and all the pus is removed, then pour or wash with clean and cold water or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wound does not heal and moisture enters the palace, if it does not penetrate as it should, there is a bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting: therefore, you must go to the end of a piece of linen, and sew with our hands, and leave a space between each stitch of an inch or less; and put the bad parts of the thread into the wound through the mouth; and draw out as it comes out through the mouth inside the mouth; and many times they do this to children at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the head that comes out of the mouth with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and sew them together as we are who are or thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you see that the hairs have not rotted that part, then remove the filth, soak in blood, and rub the cloth into an Egyptian plaster, and put it back on the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the plasters corrode all that remains of the part; then put on the nose a piece of leather for several days until it is healed, and if there is need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the nose, with which one distills oils and medicines onto the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a snout, and hold it thus; and if you see, make a closed snout, and let the instrument be plain for purifying the nose; and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the sinus headache
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Frequently, a disease arises in the sinus headache that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large over time; and for this reason, you should cover it at the beginning, and completely remove the cause, then apply the fire cautery or the burning medicine; and if they delay in covering it until it is large, if it is hard, of poor color, and insensitive: if you do not touch it with iron, because it is an infected abscess, because when it is covered once, then great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is softly touched, not with iron, and you see that it can be completely covered, then remove the pain and cure the limb of things that are similar and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the bone is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	However, when the solution comes in one of these cartilaginous places, it is of little use, as it is not beneficial to everyone.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound is fresh and full of blood, look at whether the lips are swollen on both sides; then apply the II leaves to a seam, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already decayed on one side or the other, you must scorch all the parts of them that are not healed, then bring the two lips together at a seam, hold them, and powder with powder of blood of dragon and frankincense; and put the powders on a piece of strong or other plaster, and let it heal through it, then treat the wound with an ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is such that you gather the edges: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses inside the lips, which are hard and small or large; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut each one, and take the pus with tweezers and clean each part; then apply the wound after the incision of ground glass, until the wound is not stained; then apply ointment, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the crown of the teeth
