Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a crown of the teeth grows above the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to hold it with forceps at its base, and cut off the gum or the pus; then put on the tooth a powder of broken glass, or other powders that are astringent and desiccative; and if this crown returns after the incision, and often does, cover it again and cauterize: if it does not return after the cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments to cover.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, the roots of teeth are gathered at the chief of the tooth, between the gums, and sharp, unpleasant scorches; and sometimes, the teeth are black, yellow, and green, until corruption reaches the gum, and they are also stinking teeth. So, you should put the bad thing between your hands, and its roots should be in your holy place, and pull out the teeth or the scorches that are visible, until nothing remains; and thus, make the black, yellow, green, and yellowish, and other stains, until they are cleaned. And if you remove what is at the first level, it is good; but if not, start again from the second day and the third, until you have removed everything. Also, know that teeth have a variety of shapes of tools for scraping, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scraper used to scrape between the teeth has different shapes than the one used to scrape the roots of the teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating a toothache that you delay removing it for as long as possible, because no one should do this; for it is a very high substance, from which there is no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the toothache is extremely painful, you should be certain that the tooth is dead.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the toothache deceives one into thinking it is a holy tooth, and you remove the good tooth; and then the pain does not disappear because of this, for we have already done this to such saints; and when you are certain that the tooth is dead, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth in all directions; then press it with your fingers or subtle pliers at the first point and point, until it is well dislodged, then firmly fasten the pliers; and let the one who has the toothache in your holy mouth between your teeth, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, take one of these tools and push it gently into each part lightly, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the holes are; and if the extraction is subtly held by hooks, so that it does not break when extracting; and it is very important to cover around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part, and again cause the pain by the evil of the root more great pains of the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant who, due to their haste and recklessness, break the chariot every time, and never amend what we have told; but bring forth only once through the quackery of disease for the roots that they delay, or for the chariot that they break, as often as we have seen; and when the dense matter is drawn out, wash the limb with wine or vinegar and silk; and if blood flows, which often happens, use the wounded limb with boiled frankincense; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, by which one moves the first tooth, should be long and thick-handled, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick-bodied so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-made iron, and they should be pointed to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, then you must place a piece of clean cloth on the cheek or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	so that the cheek is not torn, then pull the hooks called "algefri", because the patient resembles a careful beak; and they should be made inside like a wedge and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out at all these needles, it is necessary that you dig around the root completely, and put the tool called "althali", which is a spoon-shaped instrument, in order to:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is too thick so that it does not break easily, and if the root jumps out of the ground, it is good; but if not, then use all the tools, from which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this tool that has two prongs, with which comes the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the realm of the teeth, and with this tool that looks like large needles, from which comes the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be used only when it cannot be broken, and sharp that many of the instruments of dense are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned here; and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease indicates, for there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of them, and if they broke the cart or other bones, or if they hurt, if they look for instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let the bones be large and well-held to keep them in place, so they do not escape, but that it can hold and remove; then restore the limb with medicines suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, if the surgeon has all these tools:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in line with the natural course of the jaw, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you remove the tooth if it is nestled after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and no one can be or lime: then the ray; and if it is with the tooth, take this tool which has the shape of a small beak, and is similar to a small hook made of iron and sharp:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper bit by bit in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be removed, then the copper bit by bit like this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the copper of which arrows are made; and in the tooth bit by bit in your hands lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks; then the plain at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, then you must remove the roughness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when they are missing
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth are missing, either by percussion or falling out, and the gums cannot press up against the space where they used to be, and you have tried medicines that do not work, then you should bind them with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never does; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are moving, take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the missing teeth between the healthy ones, if there is one or more, until you feel them securely against the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the covering towards the part where you started, and gently and skillfully press your hand, so that it does not move at all; and let your wire be tied to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the broken teeth and fasten them with wires, and assemble them, and place them between the sound teeth, and so that they do not break the tongue; and then leave them so tight as they can hold, and if they dislodge, or the wire breaks, then fasten them with another wire; if it holds, it will serve in this way throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the appearance of the bridging of two sound teeth, and of two broken ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth breaks, if you put it back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and do not interfere with it unless it is wise and painful, and never once has anyone made the form of a bone tooth of a cow, and you put it in the place where the defect is, and fasten it as we have said, and hold it and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is this ligament which comes from the tongue or by nature, that one is born like this; or by accident of a wound; and the works are such that you cut the tongue's hurt, and hold its head in your sound, and relieve the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or not, and it is from a severe wound, if you boil the wool and cut widely, gently; and be careful that the wound does not bleed too much, for the artery which is out; and when you have done, lift the tongue with high rose and vinegar, or high cold, then put away from the tongue a linen tent; and treat the hurt every night, so that the wounds cannot stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood flows out, place the wounded part on a broken piece of glass; and if it does not stop bleeding, cauterize it with slow-burning charcoal, which is good for the wound; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is of a yellow or black or hard color, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is chancre; and if it is declining towards discharge, and there is moisture, pour water through a narrow-mouthed vessel, and deliver it from both sides; and if it does not stop bleeding at your first attempt, place the wounded part on a broken piece of glass until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you have treated all the wounds. Then lift the limb out of its socket and treat with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No time comes from within the throat boils that are called "godath", and they are properly called the II amnions, and when you cure them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if they are hard and small in size and of a dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, just as for the discharge of blood; but let it remain until it dies, and then you will break it off, or it would break by itself; and if it is of a white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check if the throat abscesses are at rest and are calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head is in a healthy position, and the operation tool is held between his hands, and press the tongue away from all the instrument, which is its form; and it should be made of silver or fine brass like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and the hook in the ambre, and draw it out above as much as you can; and take nothing else with, then cover the tool with a cloth, which has the form of a forceps; and all the while the head is bent, and one place another, and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, with a hook, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, and on the other part, name; and when you have hooked one of the hooks, hook the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sharp pain with hot and cold water, and if there is blood flowing, gargle the sharp pain with hot water, or use pounded green pomegranate skins, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleaned; then care for it until it is healed; and never do other abscesses come out of the throat except the two hooks, if they are then hooked in this way.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged deep within her throat, specifically a small abscess; and she had almost entirely closed off her entire throat, such that the woman could not breathe at all due to the swelling, nor eat or drink, and died if she remained so for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been inserted with two needles through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore acted quickly, and inserted one needle into the nostril, then removed the majority of the pus; then I inserted another portion through the other nostril, and pressed on the tongue to keep the mouth open; after inserting the needle into these abscesses, I removed a part, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus the woman's breathing was restored in her throat, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; the abscess grew again, and filled up the cavity that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I inserted a seton into her throat: thus she did not grow worse; and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When referring to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, and you see that the abscess is calm, and it is thin, then you must lance it; and the one that is round and not long; and if it is bloody or dark red or black, then you must avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger in the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its breadth and length, that you make the hair sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the tool that we have mentioned before; then insert the needle into the vein, and draw out the blood, and close it with one or two of the tools that I have mentioned in the incision of the two arrows.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not close more than the excess which is beyond the natural end; for if you close more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use the remedy that we have mentioned in the incision of the two arrows, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is too great for the copper, then you must use an engine for the cauterization of the sensitive pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauterization is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on your sound shoulder, and then presses his tongue against the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and applies with very hot, live iron, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in making this movement of the instrument, which is in this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the head have a hair or object to put the medicine on, like the movement of a spoon, and puts the instrument all the medicine over the gum; and the patient lies on his side, so that saliva and mucus from his mouth flows into the medicine inside, so that it does not drip down his throat and blood; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it over the gum, for a quarter of an hour, until you see the medicine is working and the effects of the medicine are relieved; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument through all the cotton on top, until the cotton is burned over the gum; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then let it dry for four days or five. And if you have the skill to begin again with the cauterization of the medicine, then begin again, and after the cauterization, wrap it around the gum with moist cotton, and clean what is around the medicine; and be rubbed with hot water, and be treated with gargling until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer from incision than from cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take sage and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and all or some of them in a pot, and put oil in it, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the pot there should be an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the instruments should be inserted in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is dead; afterwards, it is repeated often, until the eye is dry, and guard that you do not make heat at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess chaut, for many things happen; and do not make heat except at the declination of the abscess chaut.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If this instrument is not present, take a sponge and place it inside the mouth, so that the patient's mouth does not choke; for the sponge does not cause the vapor to oppress the mouth, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often one must remove bones or fish spines from the throat, or nothing at all; therefore, you must take out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun at all times with the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open and is returned to the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit the bad thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is removed by vomiting; or the bad things swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes back to the throat, it will stick, and then pull out firmly; and if it does not come out because of what we have said, take the instrument from the bottom in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the curved instruments be bent at the head so that they can more lightly enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that nothing comes out, or push too much of the bone inside; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, because it is softer or the thing is sharp; if it goes down, or it pulls it all the way through the instrument evenly, as far as it goes.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat wound
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no cure for the throat wound, as I said in the division, by the care of medicines; and if it does not improve, then look at the wound in the throat to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sandal, take it to all the small nails, or with thin needles that are worth for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, take a hairy rope, and push it into the throat of the misaligned joint, then push or move the rope with the sharp iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the misaligned joint is stiff all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it down to swallow, and move it to your hand often; and as soon as the sandal feels the cold, it drops.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not smell as we have said, of the stench of garlic, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will eventually disappear.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation is such that you hold a pot with charcoal in it, and place a cloth covering in the middle, and in this pierce the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the head of the snake in its mouth, and close its mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes to its nose; and the nose will now be clear, and if it does not clear, you must repeat the fumigation many times; and suffer the snake to be thirsty, and give it things to eat and drink, and do not let it drink water; and then it will have the matter to pass through this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used to treat the sinew is, when one can see it, similar to curved tongs for entering the throat; and it resembles a beak of care, and it has roughness of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscess, according to what the memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in puncture and incision; and it is in two ways that one is in its own appearance, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the bones or when they are broken.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the thigh bone are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if abscesses are to be pricked in which one should not pierce until the swelling is completed; and if of those that it is necessary to pierce when they are crusted, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is swollen around, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located deep within the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it has died, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located deep in the foundation, if you pierce it too late, it will not be able to bear weight, and will remain crooked inside, and there may develop a fistula; and it cannot be healed in the long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you remove the pus from the abscess perforation according to its completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the reduction of fever, and the lessening of pain and swelling, and the diminution of debility and agitation of the main part of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens most; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the position of that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the chest, it is better to leave the incision until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, it may spread along the vein of the arm, and cause much filth; and perhaps harden the lips and penetrate into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the arm, according to what the limb has need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is appropriate to drain small abscesses with small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the shape of the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses or it is necessary to cover them, and cover; when it has become as the cloth, and is softened, it is appropriate to do as one does with bubbles: and if such abscesses that are cut in three angles, and if such abscesses that one covers like the flank of a mule, as abscesses of arrows; and if such abscesses where one makes a round shape, and other shapes and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, if the abscess is superficial, it is necessary to lance it clearly; and if the abscess is large, and has great swelling, and you lance it, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then stop the abscess the next day, then remove nothing else; do this gradually many times, until the pus is all out; especially if the wounds are of weak virtue, or women carrying, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced never treats the wound once with the outflow of the pus, because by chance the abscess may die, and you will not be harmed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, dry the wound, and see if the abscess wound is small; and if a tailor complains, soothe him with linen or woolen cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you fill each one with linen or cotton cloth against each other; and if you have covered part of the skin in the abscess, and you have wrapped it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or rags of linen against moisture, and bind it to the wound; then open, and treat the dressing until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is blood when working on your task, apply sharp cold and wet, and clean the instrument, and place it on the dislocated joint multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocated joint persists, and if it is governed and treated, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book are at hand, and if it is very painful, and if the wound or abscess is very nervous, then you should put on tents and clean cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it is in a bad state, and the wound is charred, then you should put on clean cloths soaked in cold and hot water, or in warm and cold wine, as we have said; and then drain the abscess, dress it, and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	des soros
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, and there are ways of them that are in cloths, like the lance of a swallow, and many there are.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also large and such ones that have moisture like fish; and there are some that are hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cut is such that you prove with all the tool called "entromissoire", from which the form comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	If it contains moisture, then it makes it from above downwards long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off any hair that contains that moisture, because it will return if you leave anything; then soak cotton in Egyptian oil, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it there until the next day; and this will continue what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, the second day, and the wound, until you are sure it will not remain at night; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess remains large, then cover it with this form, long; and pour in ointment, and scrape off the skin from all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it is; and if the artery opposes, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And so do with the abscess if it is piercing, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting into the piercing abscess and the moist, it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and are of the kind I copied or of an old woman; and found the abscess also like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had cut into it, they would have made as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, because those who come to the head of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent part, so that the pus can drain out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of tumors
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times there are abscesses at the neck, and they are removed with forceps, and then they are opened, and sometimes they come from other parts of the body or chest, and they are large, and they are joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each tumor is properly on its side, like the one and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these tumors are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some things that contain moisture, and if there are evil ones who do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see in good position at the touch, and resembles the color of the flesh, and moves from each part and is not merged with the nerve or the artery or the conduit, and is not deeply; then it is necessary to cut from above, and scrape each part, and hold the two lips of the wound as one, if you have experience, as we have said in the chapter on abscesses; and gradually and gently, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not make it too small or too deep, so that the hands do not escape, and do not see too much before, that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you open it, put vitriol broth or some powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and begin to poultice.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is clean, return to your work, until you complete it; then check your index to see if there are any small pustules remaining, and cut and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has a large vein at the base of the pustule, you should not cut that pustule at its base, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through it without causing harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have completely removed the scab, it is necessary that you gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, then as there is no excess due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	and you should cover the root of it with a bandage and pull out the thorn, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scabs that have excess, pierce where it apertures to die; and pierce in such a way as the one previously mentioned, depending, then apply ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well dressed, if the cure of ointment enjoining charcoal, until it is healed.
de squinance	of the dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the torturer of the throat; but I never saw one in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have dislocation, the furrow of the throat which is called "epiglottis" must be avoided; and it cannot be helped by this, because all veins and the pore of the bad wound are in those who have abscesses full in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it out of three circles or four, with a small cut across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the sharp edge, not in the cartilage; and those are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no char, and the vessels are long and do not bleed.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the neck all around, then cuts the throat until it reaches the windpipe; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the sharp edge, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the windpipe which springs forth from the bone that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which we doubt strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and cover it completely with gauze; then administer medicines that cause vomiting until they are cleansed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this unless the throat is completely stunned, and the limbs are judged to be dead, and the defect is paralyzed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, one should cover the epiglottis for this reason that the limbs cannot move, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and because they commanded the ancient one to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And therefore, they commanded to sew the wound and heal, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife, and stabbed herself in the throat, and cut part of the windpipe down; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not bled much from the vein except for the throat, and the blood flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and closed the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and she did not die because she was called back to life, and returned to her usual condition; for I believe that in the sewer of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of a grape, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally without any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental way is in two ways: one is similar to a large goiter, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us through the artery; and there is fear, and it does not need to be opened except by a small incision, and the proof and search are made throughout the entire insertion: if you find it as in the large one, and cannot be cut at all, if the skin, if as in the large one, and if there is no skin, take it all at its own cost, and examine it well and treat it as it should be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	We have many ways of doing things, of which I will say all the similarities; but now it is necessary for me to tell all the difference between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that they are cold and feverish, until the ebullitions have passed, and it is accomplished by purgation; then the fever and cold subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us, there is neither cold nor fever nor pain, and it contains the spleen, which is its own organ and is according to the color of the blood, and begins like a grape, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either dry or moist, and much of the color is as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when coming to the care of a new patient, to first test and inquire about the "entromissoire" instrument, according to its form as it appears in the following chapter or book.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you press or more moist skin than you pierce into the abscess, and gradually return your fingers, until you know that the instrument has pierced through the bottom, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the "entromissoire", and be careful not to cause harm.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the wound is wet and has a certain color, make it so as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision moisture does not come, scrape it if it is greasy, then make a cross incision, and take pincers and scrape lightly from every part and wash the coat or where it was with new water; and if you cannot remove it cleanly, scrape it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, it returns to us many times; and if it stays for a short time and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, keep the wound closed, and use other remedies until it is healed; and if it is large, cut out the two lips of the wound, and cure what remains with char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if you feel it beating against you, or any other thing that hurts and hastens you, take the vinegar bottle and pour it into the wound, leaving it there for two hours or three, until the pain subsides, and then remove the clotted blood; then return to the copper that was left behind.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See the forms of the instruments used for extraction, and there are three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret," and one is called "breb," and there are also three ways: large, medium, and small, to search for the stones in fistulas; and they are also like the needles that are used for sutures, and they are made of brass yellow, or iron, or silver, and they cost as much as those that are already yellow, and they are more useful for removing the corbeurs in fistulas; and there are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the fistula.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the nails are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are nails with two teeth in three ways; and there are nails with three teeth, and they are also in three ways; and there are nails with two teeth, and a single tooth nail, and they are also in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The main tools used for these purposes are sharp, and there are some that do not cut except from one part, from which we scrape the hairs, because they do not cut the vein or the nerve; and of these intruments are the almoners placed in spoons, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses only a smaller one in the fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and joints, and similar places; and never is used any other instrument small, resembling scrapers for drawing blood, according to this form, with which we open veins.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never placed back into its proper position which can cope with veins, and arteries, and it always returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as they seem like breasts of women; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form of this line b. until g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is soft like women, and if it is in the ribs above, because of similar tears; because one holds the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line b. until the line g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the pain does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with moistened cotton in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the ankles
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the ankles are ways of hard scrofula or when there are pustules, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and care for the wound with a poultice until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, then cut them as we have said in incisions of scrofula, and if the wound does not heal, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the tearing of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is torn, and the skin above it is discolored, then often abscesses occur, and just as much blood flows from the vein; and if you know it is for the artery, then cut the abscesses longwise; and when you feel it with your fingers, if it is to one side, hold it steady; and when it is for the vein, then cut it open from below; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside the bones and muscles and other parts, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one who is in charge should also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen from an artery fainting through the skin on top; then open the abdomen with incisions, and gently separate the artery from the flesh until it is exposed; then insert a needle on the other side, and pierce it with another needle on the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread according to what I have shown in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not pull the flesh that is between the two threads of an intromission until the missing part is revealed, and remove the abscess; then treat the wound as it was injured, as long as the wound heals; and if the abscess is for the belly of the vein, if you dip your hand in what comes out of the abscess to all the skin, then pull the needle out of the flesh that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and there should be a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or one of the two threads of the needle at the incision of the first needle, and if you doubt that the thread will not fit, then insert another needle all the way through the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cover the abscess until the excess is removed, then cover the wound and leave what is left; then put a piece of moist cloth on it with wine and oil, then treat the wounds of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the neck
