Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come to the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the neck when it is cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And there are often abscesses and doubts in all the limbs where there are joints, and this is the greatest grief, and its color resembles the color of the blood, and it is in many positions with pain; and when one stretches it, if the patient feels great pain, and it is not in the front of the body, but outside the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and those who are in joints do not need to be covered with iron: perhaps there is contraction; and those who are in the head or face, making the skin thin.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have needles, and prick it at its root; and if it is large, if you suspend it from a hook, and scrape it, then remove the bone and stitch the wound together at the seam, and cure it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large jaws hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never found in bellies and never in any other part of the body, and it is a disease called "funge" by its resemblance to worms, and it has subtle roots, and large jaws; and there are both small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or three bellies that were more like funges than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had subtle roots, and were torn, and it was filled with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces heavy, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the artifact is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper has a wide spatula, and they are in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the cutting, there often comes too great disturbances of blood, and if you do not see the hair extending and painful from the incision of the iron, take the thread of good quality, and tie the artifact as we have said, and leave it for two hours; then restrain, and do not cease to straining the thread of good quality until it covers the artifact, and cut through it with work; and if the roots are large, put the copper itself on the belly, but you must well copper half, then cauterize that it does not return; then care for the wound, and guard that you do not cover the thigh which is of pale color and poor sensation and of light regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these abscesses are infected, and I will come to the treatment of pus afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is deep
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound comes from the cauterization of a wound or the cutting of a tendon, and it is above the belly and in some of the abscesses, as it has in other wounds, of blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of pus; and if it is from the tearing of the syfac and from the exit of the pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides so it returns, and then it comes back, and perhaps if it is torn, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, then it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not force much; and if it is for arrows, if it is open by these signs of the abscesses being large and hard, and is filled with a quantity; and if it is for windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look to see if it appears to be for the arrow of the vein, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boueil, then you must command the patient to dye his alaine, and be stretched straight out, then sign around the belly; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have indicated all the way through the spatumile, then stretch half of the abscess up over the great sinew; then tie it around with a strong silk thread, or a firmly tied rope, and let the other end loose; then open half of the abscess stretched over the rope, and you must insert your finger, and draw out the intestine; if you pull out the rope, then tie it back, and draw out the intestine from behind the belly; and if you pull out the boueil, then take it at the base, and cut away the excess; and if the artery makes it go against, or the vein, then go around slowly, then return to your work and take two needles, and draw out two threads of silk, and insert the two needles as you have done in order to pierce; then stretch the abscess into four pieces over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the limb as long as it can bear, and cut off the dead flesh by itself; or you take it when it has become thin and ready to burst, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and suture the abscess as we have said; then draw out the pus or the moisture that you have removed, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and soak the limb.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization,
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken in the division of the similarities of chancre, and how one must act with medicines, and how one must observe the care of iron; and we say that chancre is engendered in the mouth, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancients said that when chancre is in a place where it can be removed as chancre which is in the breasts, and in the armpits, and in similar places, and one must remove everything when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, if one does not need to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any of them; and no one has ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in the place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge once the hairs of black pus; then make it clean if it has manifest repletion, then wipe the hair and the skin of all parts, and leave nothing; and let the blood flow freely, and wipe the part well with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding does not stop, do not make the incision of the artery or vein, and cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydrocephalus
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the previous section about the similarities of hydrocephalus, and how the assembly of the acute is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment that is done by medicines, and that which is treated by iron: if it is only swollen; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hypsarche, for it is a fatal matter; therefore when you treat this similarity of hydrocephalus which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the treatment does not help, if you look at whether the pain is weak, or if he has another disease besides hydrocephalus, as in all cases and solution of the stomach and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the pain is very strong, and he has no other disease except hydrocephalus alone, and he is not too old or too young, then thus: lift up the pain straight across your hands, and the assistants press the belly by pushing the acute to the lowest part of the worst, then take the spatula in the shape of this:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cutting of two parts at the tip, and ensure that no part is too thin so that it can reach the intestines when thrown, and cannot be bleached; then look if there is hydrops towards the intestines: if it is necessary to make a cut of three fingers' breadth from the left side of the belly; and if it is for the disease of the liver, then the incision should be on the right side of the belly; and if it is for the gallbladder, then it should be on the right, and it is not necessary that the hairs grow on the incision so that the superfluous do not run to the weakest part; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and squeeze, and remove your hand from all the space between the skin and the gallbladder as if when scraping a quantity of an inch or around; then pierce the gallbladder until the space reaches the desired length, and that is the legs of the gallbladder, then remove it with this instrument of which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is similar to a silver coin, subtle and thin, made of light lead or chalk, and has small holes in its middle part; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and it is shaped like a pen, and this is the form of the incision that the scribes make for the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of this instrument is the awl, so that when the instrument comes to the skin, it should be placed on top of the instrument; therefore, leave the remaining or third part, because if you remove more than necessary in that hour, by chance if the pain dies from the resolution of its spirit from the weapon, or it falls asleep, or it approaches death; but according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the pain mean, and its pricks; then remove the instrument and retain the point, which is now stopping the hole that is above the eyebrow, of which I have spoken, that you should prick in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the pain suffering, and take a small quantity of the point; do this every day, and be careful not to remove more than a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the pain, and you leave it for a long time, then the cure of the sepulchre or sand bath, and by much sweating or bathing in the sun, and if it becomes tainted from drinking; and the cure of desiccative medicines until it is healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the arrow, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the staff
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born who does not have a cord in the staff, or the cord is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to prick often with a very thin needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place or puncture the thin silk thread underneath, and bind it and tie it thus for three or four days, and when it wants to urinate, if possible, open the closure, let it urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not suitable, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is punctured is small, then treat it with a thin silk thread as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the puncture in their leg are bled, because no one is born with a puncture at the top of the thigh, which prevents them from urinating before their thigh opens; and they cannot urinate because the matter cannot come up to the marrows, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs lie evenly on their backs, the chief of the staff and the cap are as wide as the shaft of a feather, so that the puncture is made in the middle, as it should be; and guard against the evacuation of blood which often comes, and if it does, use the same bandage as for bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the staff
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often come boils in the staff, and it is an ugly appearance; and there are both good and bad ones; if it is necessary to prick them at once with a fine needle, cover and clean all of them, then put on Egyptian moist cotton dressing; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if it is a bad dislocation, with a putrid color and smell, then you must apply the fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cleaned it, and if the dislocation is in the joint, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must first reset the part that is inside; and when it is set, then care for the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, do not be sure that the joint is not perforated, and it becomes black and corrupted in its joint and where the bone is; then remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply the ointment of honey and flour which is made from the shells of grenades and nuts, then care for other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes out, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization tools should aid in the following two situations: when blood comes out and when corruption occurs; and if the part of the staff is corrupted and drawn back, then it is necessary to drive or place a cloth soaked with plaster between the wounds, and urinate on the painful parts; and when the flesh has grown at the top of the staff, which has not been circumcised before, or if there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to scorch it with the tool until the flesh is separated from the staff, and deliver the part of the staff from all sides; and if this is a difficult matter to decide, then it is necessary to scorch it with the spatula at any point from the top of the staff and the skin, then thoroughly clean between them, and place a subtle linen cloth soaked in cold milk on it, so that it does not grow again.
de la circoncision	For circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our will, and properly in children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not direct circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of the masters and the sages who performed circumcision in the Middle Ages, and as forces, and at all one generation; since it was the choice because it had two threads, and by chance if one cuts the other above and delays that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is prolonged, and the pain is doubled, and the wound healing which is done by the time is not assured at the point of the member; and the wound healing of the angle by chance escapes the iron, and corrupts the work, and many times it is born in such a way that they have no need of healing and I have seen.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound healing which is done by force to all the length of the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all the length of the thread; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and that the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he listens, that you do not make him fasten the thread around the rod only, and then throw it in all the ways that you can; then make it lie between your hands straight, and bring the forces between your hands or outside your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand on the rod and blow or suck, and take it up as high as the part of the rod is clean; then wipe well the dirt that is gathered there, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it outside to the other thread; and keep it between two fingers by the second work at the pouch and at the right index, and cover between the two threads, then lift the upper quickly and take the head of the rod; then let the blood drip slowly and slowly, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on top and on top of the powder a poultice made of a moist cloth cooked with rose water tempered with red wine vinegar and oil rose and fresh, and let it rest on the other side, and cure the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for the purification is thus: the two shoulders are tense and are thrusting, and are also the same as the chest equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the fist is inside the incision; therefore, it must be extended to your elbow, also when the legs have an abscess; and the coping equally, and if you cannot hold it at your elbow, then use nails, and then the coping.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they have passed three days, and what is outside the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscess has subsided, and scrape lightly; and the coping as you can move, and guard from the part of the rod, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the patient of things unclean wounds of powder, which we have said or treated for powders, and if one takes too much care, it goes above, if not harmful; therefore treat as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the compression of stones, or blood congealed, or bowels, or intestines, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not discharged, and you see the retention due to the stone which is high or near the bladder, it is necessary that the pains are raised above their knees; and they are placed on their feet on the back, and extend their belly from the part above the back, and restrain the pains as much as possible; and thus the bladder is pressed against the stone above, for which reason the urine is discharged; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the pains are great, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it should be thin silver hair, like a quill of an owl; and it should be the tail of a palm length and half, and it should be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the thread to the top of the cloth or cotton, and pull the head of the thread into the tube; and wipe the excess cloth and pull it towards the top of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on the seat, and place the penis and the moistened oil and olive oil and vinegar; then place the tube heavily on the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the tube over the top; then pull the tube forward just before the cloth, and feel the patient coming towards the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide or she goes is twisted; then stop the thread at each little cloth piece by piece, and the urine follows the cloth, then remove it, and correct the urine; and start again until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood comes into the bladder, and there is putrefaction and assembly, and you see distillation of waters and medicines, then do all the instrument that is called «clepsedre», and it is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads are passed through it by means of which the medicine is poured in so that it touches the bladder well without addition, so that they can draw out the urine, and put it wherever it is needed; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the urine, and pull out the tube which is on the side; then draw out the urine through the catheter, and put back the tube strongly on the side; then the urine will enter the tube, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it. And this is the form of the subtle cloth with which they catheterize the bladder: if it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is made of silver or copper, and is the highest of the two; and from there to the breast where the joints are located; then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you see has clogged the bladder, then place it between the two breasts with a good strong thread doubled, and heat the moisture above the fire; then pour the head of the poultice into the stick, then strain your hand on the bladder all around the moisture, until the hairs feel that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then tighten the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a wheel, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the methods of stone and extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone embedded in rain, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should make an incision; and in the bladder, and in the staff; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder resembles a sharp pain in its subtlety; and it has hair, and great pain in the staff, and it happens many times, and then it becomes round; and at the end of these jumps, the foundations; and it is light for the healing of children up to the age of four, and it is very painful in old people, and it is a constant problem for those who are between young and old; and it is a lighter cure for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with chalk, to draw out all the impurities that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never obstructs one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand up and move it towards the outside, so that the stone descends to the edge of the anus, and never once rises above the thigh; then place it between your hands and prepare it, with your hands away from your thighs, so that the intestines are all declining downwards; then remove and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not chew at all, then moisten your index finger of the right hand, if the pain is sharp, or your middle finger, if the pain is dull; and place it on its base, and strike the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the area where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the anus with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand to the testicles above, and his left hand to remove the skin that is outside the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then cut the spatula-shaped part, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And making between what is between the ribs and the foundation, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval; and it should be straight up the spine, and its end should be at the foundation or the bottom, and its tail should be across so that it is wide by lack, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the spine, not too large; perhaps the pressure on the end which is at the foundation, that it may jump out without effort; and if there are pieces of bone or angles, and edges: if they are rough to extract; and if there are pieces which are smooth, like a glass, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When there are angles and margins where it should be cut, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump, then it is necessary to strain it with nails that are as thick as a lime at the top, to prevent the stone from escaping; or you can use a subtle hooked instrument at the top; and if you cannot engage it in this way, then enlarge the opening slightly, and if there is no decortication, then strain it with vinegar; and if there are more than one stone, then first remove the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut it off, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it should be made larger, and a larger wound should be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it dies, or the urine comes out through the skin that the leeches cannot seal; but nevertheless you must try to draw out, or tear with pincers, until you remove it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and place a moist cloth on top of it, in oil and wine, or in oil and vinegar and cold vinegar, to soothe the boil; then resolve the wound over its collarbone, and do not leave the bandage until the next day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, rise the joint well with oil and vinegar, then apply ointment of mustard plaster and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	If abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and is held by such retention of urine, which is known in a certain way that without sound with urine: then put your hand on the wound, and remove that blood, because if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and pollute; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and oil, and assist him in all ways that you can, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the remedies that you cure him with, that you bind his two thighs, and gather the medicines above the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the arrow is small and it is conducted with a stick, and tied up, and the urine cannot come out; then the cure that I have said before, that you cut many times, is to excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and be at three angles tied in one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie the wound around the stick outside the arrow, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then lightly beat the iron on the stick until it reaches the arrow; and slowly turn the iron in your hand on the arrow bit by bit, until you can pierce the arrow from the other side; then soon the urine will come out, then press your hand above where the part that is remaining of the arrow which is inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is already broken, and has jumped with the urine, and is sharp to the hairs; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then take a piece of cloth from below the stone and another from above, then make the staff in the middle of the stone between the two pieces, then extract it forcefully, and remove the piece, and clean the blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare that a stone is inserted into women, and if it ever happens, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-trained to undress herself at will, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is further forward than the man's, because it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessary, go to the woman, so it is necessary that you grasp a needle well-versed, and with the thread, and if you do not sew, point does not ask for the cast mire subtle; and present a wise midwife in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command of the examination of the stone; and look very well if the woman is virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her foot or foundation and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she constrains it out of her foundation, and recommends that she put her foot or with the pain, and press and press her right hand firmly on the bladder form.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it from great to great from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut across the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the belly where it is muscle-covered and feels the arrow in that part; and do not move her above the bone or below, and let the tailor make a small opening; then push the arrow through the wound until it can be removed, and know that many kinds of arrows are: that is to say, small and large and sharp and blunt, long and round and straight and curved, and those with rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know, then put the similar broken glass in the wound, and keep it there for an hour until the wound is clean; then return to your work, until the stone is fully formed, and have the instruments that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone, as helpers for your work; and if you do not know, and it is the artery that is cut, then put powder on the wound and bandage with tents and bandages, and do not restart, and leave the stone and do not remove it, unless by chance the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound has healed, return to your work, until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	of umbilical hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white skin, which is outside the covering of the intestines, which contains the urine; and it is called «syfac», and never properly in the membrane of the urine, if one wishes that it be another urine; and this is the skin of the intestine between the white skin that we have said; and it does not have such a thing.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is weakness that comes to bones, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the bones, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a declining color to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and there are more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white and flat as we have said, then it is the abscesses, not long, like an egg, and does not open the bones, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own tissue, then it is the abscesses with part of an egg, and because one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the white flat, then it feels bad; therefore when you see the color of the moisture, try all the previous forms.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to how much power and the replenishment of its body; then place it on its back, on something a little high, and cover it with much cloth; then bend its right side, and command the minister to bend its left, and extend the staff to one of the two ribs near the kidneys; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the kidneys between the long and the kidneys above; and let your cut be straight in dividing the skin of the kidneys towards the white fat, and scrape the thin skin according to how much power; then pierce the white fat plain from high to wide with a sharp and large hole, and extract all the sharp, and then put your forceps, and press the white fat above; and do not touch the kidneys except the white fat itself; scrape all or in pieces evenly the side of it subtly, that if you do not scrape it well enough, it will return to the sharp; and if the white fat breaks off in your work, then replace it in its place when you have completed the work of the white fat; then gather the two flaps of the kidneys at one stitch, then cure it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you have successfully removed the splinter that has become corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubt of the flow of blood; then cut off the coagulum from the entire suspended area, and remove the splinter, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the bone is assembled in two parts, it is because there are two branches; then treat the other part as you have done the first evenly, then suck out the blood, and apply a poultain of rose oil on the wound; and place another poultain of linen and oil in wine on top of that, and cover the two wounds with doubled cloths, and bind it all together according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and place them with linen gauze according to this similarity and gathered by sewing at the waist of the drawers, and the one from the patient taken above the base just below the back, and the other at the part of the elbow; and the other head above the two angles, and all together the restriction in the loop of the drawer; and once this branch of the cautery is medicated in the shape of an iron tail, and it is that you take one cauterizing needle fine, and cover the skin of the wounds, and it is heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing the inflammation is revealed; then take the cautery according to this form, and perforate that pus with small holes, and the skin with this subtle cauterizing:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And in all ways that you can, until you extract everything; and guard that the flesh does not touch the bone; and cleanse this work so it is safer; and guard against the evacuation of blood, and make sure that the operation goes well; and if nothing goes against you, or an abscess forms or bleeding occurs or something else, then cure what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the hairs are painful and do not want to endure this work due to its horror, then use perforation, as I have told you, and it is that when you are sure by the signs that we have said that the sharp edge is laid, then place the painful part on the raised seat; then perforate the abscess in the part farthest from everything wide, and place the perforation at the long end of the body; and let the wounds be wide so that all the sharp edges are removed; then put cotton on the wound and bind it, and leave to drain the remaining sharp edge, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the sharp edge issue from the mouth of the wound, then you must push a needle or the instrument with which the sharp edge of the hydrops was treated, of which the form is as before; and enlarge the wound, and let the sharp edge return, and is assembled after six months or within, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the hairs will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscess of the jaws
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	For in the section of this branch, many people die because it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and similar things about the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the teeth and even from the jaws; and it is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excessive sharp and cold, which is spread in the jaws, or from impact; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of blood; and it does not cause pain, and it is a painful abscess; and perhaps it is some gray and poisonous and yellowish abscesses, and of foul color, and sometimes comes from a wound or from an infection of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from the artery, it is known by the high position of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it should not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of opening a vein are known by their position at the gentle touch of the fingers, and can be done well with a knife on this resemblance, and on the other charms; and it is that you care for the cure of the wounds, then the wound is in the top, and the trail is from the white syringe, and deliver the suspensoire from all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already healed with these charms, then it should be that you cut the wound, and the cure; and if it is air in the syringe, or in what is inside the veins, then it should be that you deliver all of that hold, and the cure roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the shoulder blade is broken at its base, then it is necessary that you remove it entirely, and extract the bone, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your treatments are completed, apply the wound with soft linen in red oil and wine, then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a type of abscess surrounded by an envelope resembling a burdock, with the softening of the groin, and the pain is great when moving; and the cure for this disease is as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and we will tell you about its treatment, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to make the dislocated part sit on the elevated seat, then lift the suspensory ligament of the tendons down to your fingers, and all the veins that are close to the edge, and rub the masters, and extend them evenly; then cut the sharp spatula across the middle of the veins, as far as they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then take a needle or double-threaded one, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came out, and tie it on the other end; then apply the bandage evenly, straight along the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as with the others, so that none of the veins are torn; for by this no harm comes, and if all the veins come out visibly, it is necessary to draw the veins from all the limbs; so that the eyes do not lose their sight due to the incision of the veins, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are due to the section that comes out or presses on the tooth, or the extension over the abdomen in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that section to one of the kidneys; and this section is either toothache or from the extension of it, and these two methods of many causes come: by impact, by jumping, by shouting, or by lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the signs when it is the extension of the toothache, it is that it has little and little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal to the front, because the tooth is close to the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the section of the tooth, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and has various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and this is for the outcome of the intestine and the heart due to the tooth.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the worms are found with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of iron with fear, for which it is necessary to withdraw.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of the work is that you command or fear that the intestine be rolled up in your hand inside the wound, if it can be withdrawn; then place the neck above, and loosen the jaws; then press the wound together with the long piece of gauze, according to what you have for opening the wound, so that the pus can come out; then scrape the tooth that is outside the skin of the belly, until all the white tooth is exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger in the direction of the intestine, between the white tooth that is outside the skin of the belly, and between the second tooth, and behind the belly, and between the second tooth; and move it gently with your right hand inside the intestine, and place the white tooth in your left hand on top of the belly; then command the assistant to stretch the belly upwards, and remove what is behind the skin; and if you find anything, bring it out of the stomach; then take a needle or a thread made of twelve threads, and insert it into the back part of the tooth, which is after the skin of the belly; then cover the threads with the belly, and tie them in the shape of a cross, and tie the tooth, which we have said is outside the skin of the belly, of two thick pieces of two parts; then cover the threads and form them into two parts, so that no vessel that they pass through can enter the wound, that pus does not come out; and then place the first thread according to the first thread, and after these two threads leave the tooth which is outside the skin of the belly the length of one part; and then the other according to the roundness that the belly bears; then cover the part which is outside the skin of the belly, as we have said before; then apply moistened linen in oil to the wound, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white facial wound that we have mentioned, after incision, due to fear of blood clotting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the arrow remain until it has healed through it; and if it is slow to fall, then be sprinkled with hot vinegar, and put on what we have said, until it has healed; then treat the wound with other treatments, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made as the branch that is together with the viscera, in a manner that you tie the vessels, after the tail lightly to the outside; then cover it, and treat the abscess with what works, until the vessels heal; and the cure as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
