Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never come a breakage or anger, as we have said, and open the wounds; and let no one pull out any of the intestines with the fingers, and if they do, it is rare, and repair every hour; and in all ways, if it remains too long in this point, the wound believes or putsrefies, until the intestine is pulled out; and this happens by the extension of the putrefying matter which is at the breakage, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is molded and inflated the wound and opened; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have already said; and never is the cure done in this way: and it is that the hairs gently lifted from the back between your hands, then cover the wound of the breakage inflated with a large according to the quantity of three fingers; and then pull out the putrefying matter which is outside the skin that the ensues, then take the rag and place it on the wound of the breakage; and press against the front of the belly, then cut the two wounds appearing from the putrefying matter above the head of the rag, and cut both; then pull out the head of the rag, and do not cover the putrefying matter or extend the wound or other things, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the ligaments, defend and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The wound is closed, and does not appear in the tear, and the cauterization is quiet in this limb, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the shoes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of the shoes is softened in some men, because the charcoal that is inside is softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to let the wound lie flat on his back, and cut the softened leather above the natural leather; then bring the two edges together at a seam, and if you see, first remove the excess softened leather at three or four stitches; then sew between the seams, and cure it like other wounds until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	tremblingly
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is customary in our law to speak tremblingly, and because I do not wish to speak of this in this book; and it is necessary for only two reasons: the first is that the patient should respond tremblingly when asked, and be treated tremblingly; and the second, because we often have experience of trembling from certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that trembling is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, make the animal sit in high heat until the joints are softened and warm; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the cauterization of the belly: it is necessary to burn the beast, and press the skin of the intestines with your right hand, then tie the suspensory, and scrape each offal at the top, when you have well burned them; and leave no pus or subtle pus that is on the vessels; and this method of cauterization is more effective than that made by attraction, because by attraction something from the intestines remains, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	For hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are according to the second manner as men: one is that between the two intestines open like the shape of a woman's nature, with hair, and sometimes cutting the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is in women, and it is like a finger as a rod and two knives.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of the belly and the hunger is that you cut off all infected flesh, and treat it like other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays through the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tentigen
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigen is infected flesh growing above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to clean the excess of the tenting from your hand or your nails, and wipe it lightly; and not to alter too much in front, because there are no blood vessels, then the cure of other cures until they are healed; and another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and the place, and perhaps a sudden jump, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this reason they called the old "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to clean it as we have said the tenting, and the cure until it is healed.
de erratique	1. For the fire cautery, instruct
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	1. For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	2. If the patient is close and appears to be in distress, then approach them or go to them.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	3. If the patient has a subtle and sharp spine, and is close to the ribs, then hurry; place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spread her legs; then bring the two ribs together, until the subtle spine is removed, and the distress is overcome; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and place it on the wound, and bandage the woman every day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and sharp, it is necessary to apply a poultice similar to a leaf of mint.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of charcoal, then place it on the wound and cover it with medicines stained with blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and abundant oil; then apply a wide piece of cloth to prevent the wound from sticking; and thus keep it long, and then cover it with a dry linen tent; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh there comes charcoal, then cover it according to this manner, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For abscess which is in the bone, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	for hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are veins that without cutting usually bleed, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of these, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and thromboses, when they are in the bone and do not open to the touch, can only be treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the bone, which can be felt, are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then extend the altarule with clamps, and cut the cord at its roots, then apply powdered medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia and sulfur and incense, and similar things; then let her feet hang for an hour, then place her in a cold bath; if blood flows, sit her in a decoction of sumac and scrapings of green pomegranates and gall, and similar things, and then take flour of wheat, mix with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stains, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply suction cups to the back and breasts without causing harm; then take the linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of garlic with old wine, and apply to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the affected area with warmth until it is healed; and the one called «albathir» is red, and resembles a sharp chief, if it needs covering as I have said of the thelul; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marsh, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and estiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and chronic abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I mention in this treatment the abscess that comes from the marsh, which is not one of the abscesses that are boiled; and if you know how to treat with iron, look at whether the abscess is agus at the beginning of its appearance, and plain of chill and fever, and if it becomes red, then you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce, but make him wait as long as the pain is relieved; and then place the misaligned part on a chair, and have two small chairs where he leans, and rests his back on it, and gather his feet on the sides of the leg; and let his knees be spread, and put his arms away from his hips, and tie them firmly with a good belt; then apply the splint to the right side of the face, and have the instrument used to open the mouth of the jaw, from which after comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being applied, that you check the first entrance inside the instrument to see if anything enters inside that should not, and that it does not cause the misalignment; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the opening of the jaw with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt; and it is necessary that he put the horn of the instrument on top, and that he stain the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and it is done by hand, if it needs to be covered at the head, cover it with spongy leather; and when the wound is empty, put moistened tents in rose or green oil; and place the tent from the wound at the front of the marsh, and place it above the marsh and above the other clean moistened sponge in hot water; then after two hours of ointment, until it is healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound by a poultice of hot water and honey, and then of hot water or roots of lis and aristolochia are cooked; then reapply the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed in the marsh, it is necessary that you avoid cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife is first to the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman approaching, and desires to smell the ar: then hasten the child to issue; then separate that childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is its outlet with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child issues soon; for when it descends upon its head, then the secondine is with it, and is washed in the marsh of its superfluities by good cleaning; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes never above its feet, and comes fiercely upon the back or the neck, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or sometimes, and is turned over by chance onto its back, and by other bad positions; so it is necessary for the bailiff that she be wise and subtle in these things, and if she goes wrong from error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes up its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and the strength of the child is weak, then let the midwife sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and anoint her with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then give the midwife between her two fingers the smallest spatula of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And pierce the second joint, and cover it with its bone until the moisture that is inside has been removed; and take hold of the woman's belly so that the baby descends, and if it does not, then you must clisterize the woman with musk seeds mixed with sesame oil; then let her inhale and expectorate the condensed steam, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if this now causes the baby to descend.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, then you must gently and gradually reset them; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up high; then lower the chair to the ground, and tie the woman so that she does not move at the time of the raising; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the baby is dead, then cover the hands with the cloth that was previously placed there, extract the baby, and gently reset it.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes above its feet, it is necessary to place it on its back; then turn it slightly and slowly, until it is even; then take both feet and extend them slightly and slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps towards its back, command it to take a deep breath, and make it exhale from the condition; if it jumps farther, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, then turn it slowly and slowly, until it is in accordance with its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is completely straightened.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	If it does not come out as we have said, take a handful of high marjoram, and oil of sage, and melted gum, and grind everything in the mortar; and put on the natural skin of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in a high chair until above the ribs; and when she is softened out, make her a clyster of mint, and put it out, and leave it an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is now born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the birth of the child above its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, one puts his hands gently and gently on him; then it is placed on its back, and its legs are hanging down, and it is lying on the bed; and one gently folds its hands gently and gently, and then one takes its hands on its belly, and removes its clothes from below, until it is dressed downwards; and if the child does not cry, one takes its feet and forms it gently, then one moves its belly upwards, and then one blows on its face; and one feeds it little by little; and commands the woman to hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out widely a hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, then lie her on the bed, and bend her legs; then treat the muscle that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then sit her on the chair, then study to bring back the hand; and when the child is according to its natural figure, and make it suck, and command that she hold it until the child is full.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and has extended its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the ballerina stains her hand, then turns it slowly and gently; when it is even, if she has the nature of a high and oily muscle, as we have said, then command her to move slowly; and when you have done this, place it on the seat, and command her to sit; and make her spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, for all the others
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this with all the others, if the midwife can touch her face and neck, if she covers her mouth, so that she is not held back, and dies the midwife; then push the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman not to cry once: then it is born lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is often said that twins are born many times, and sometimes they are born three or four at a time; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that they do not live, if they are not named; I know why they are multiplied, and are separated by the syphilitic pox, which is caused by the umbilical cord; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one at a time, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born with great difficulty, as we have said the cure should be, and if the birth is subtle, and it does what it does quickly and lightly, then do so that it is worth doing to save life.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No children are formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, or more than fifteen months, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise one, and it is fitting that the father should examine everything, because by chance similar things happen to them; if he does so according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When caring for the woman of the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and if nothing comes out, and you are forced to manual work; it is fitting that you should examine whether the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be laid on her back, and her knees raised, and the midwife should give her two drinks of barley and of fenugreek and linseed, then wipe the mouth of the child with warm oil and musk and fenugreek and seed of lin, then rub the hands of the child with these oils and musks; then gently put the child into the mother's breast, then if she swallows the nipple that is convenient for her, and if the child is covered with sweat, and if he descends on his head; then put the nipple in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or behind the beard or in the armpit or beside the ribs, and if he descends on his feet, then put it in his hands or in his chest or in his side; and it is fitting that you tampon the nipple with your right hand, and put the cautery between the fingers of the left hand, and rub it with both hands, and put the nipple in any of these places that we have said, until the thing is empty; and this is the form of the nipple:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another one, where the patient has skill, so that the extractions are equal; and then place them equally by moving from one side to the other, to make it move, and hold the teeth with a tool like this.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, if he has some of his own oil, and put it in that part, and remove the other part; and if it does not remain, put this tool or higher up on the shoulder, and do this as much as it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and he cannot bring it back by tightening, then you must wrap it over the bandage, as long as it comes out completely; then put it in the joint of the foot or at the ankle, and so you should do in the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the patient is large and the child is narrow at the outlet, or if the head has a sharp bend, it is necessary to use the spatula-shaped instrument between your fingers, and straighten the head; or you can use the instrument called «almidach», from which the shape comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and in the same way, if the child has a large natural head; then remove the bones with pliers, and if the child's head is forced out and held at the forceps, if they are not cut, until the blood flows out; and if it cannot flow out, cover it with pieces of cloth that you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or outside the ribs, it is necessary to pierce it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the arrow is above its feet, then the light attraction is on its legs, and the advice to the mouth of the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or the groin, it is advisable to extract it with a rolled-up cloth over your hand; and if the belly or groin is injured, as long as the blood is drained; and if other members are also broken, and the patient remains conscious, if the patient's hand is brought close to the mouth of the marsh, and pulls it out of the mouth of the marsh; then bring one or two fingers, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the marsh is retracted due to an abscess that has come, it does not need to be forced, but things moist and greasy should be administered; and the ointments are applied, and in high mollifying and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If the shoulder is dislocated and it is above its place, and you can put it back in place, as we have said in the living child; and if you cannot, then remove the shoulder by pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, as we have said in the abscess cases that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be put under high pressure, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had died, then consulted the other with that one, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the armpit, and they swelled up so much that they burst open, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the patient, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong adhesive, and some bones were stuck to it, and after some time others were stuck as well.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and in it there were many bones, until the woman was much better; and she saw the woman thus for a long time, and it remained stuck with a little blood from the vein; and I had not remembered this chapter except that when masters find an unusual thing, they know how to seek help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marsh to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and then comes the form of pressure, with which one presses the books; and to two returns to two questions about two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and either made of flat or boxwood; and the mouth of the fust should be two inches wide, and the margin of the trees should be one palm and a half long; and between the two joints should be two stoppers of this same fust, which are firmly placed on both sides, half a palm or more long; and these two stoppers are inserted into the mouth of the marsh when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of an ebony or boxwood rod, according to the appearance of the forceps; and it should have two joints, as you see, about a span long, and two wide; and when you want to open the mouth with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet together and her legs spread, then push the two joints together into the mouth, and hold the handle of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the woman, until the bone does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is surmounted by all, and there are many of its kinds; and when the sick have them prepared, the more hasty the work, and the higher for humans due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise this instrument because you have not prepared it, for their need is not excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is retained at childbirth, it is necessary to command the pain to hold its fetus, and then let it expel the conditions, and hold your hands to its mouth and nose; and if it sneezes through this, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take the egg and make a small hole or cover it with a cloth, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put one or two eggs into a small hole or cover, and the other in the mouth of the marsh, and let it simmer until the steam comes out of the marsh; then make it spit out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second method does not work.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not much better, command the midwife to rub her right hand with olive oil or musk seed oil, and then put it in the natural position, and try the second method; and when she has found it, grasp it and stretch it gently and straight, so that the marsh does not tear at extraction; but move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; if it comes out and dislodges.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is narrowed, we have said the cure for vomiting and fumigation of herbs; but if there is nothing that we have said, do not force it out; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the wound, you tie to the neck of the woman, then clisterize with a healing ointment; if it will poop and be returned, and will come forth; but nevertheless, when it does so, there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and causes pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary to use the following fumigations: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to smoke the woman at the retention of flowers and the second one is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass-like appearance like a bark, and one puts the head subtly into the fire, and the smoke is over the fire; and let the fumigations be over the charcoal, and the lice until they are exhausted, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not yet pierced the foundation, but it is stopped by some subtle swelling: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that swelling at its proper place, and not to pierce it too much with a sharp instrument, and to keep the wound clean so that it does not touch it; then put on a moistened cloth in wine and oil, then the treatment of the wound until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not set, place or press a bandage of cloth, and let it remain for some time, and be sure that the child wants to go into the room.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes the swelling of a wound or abscess occurs; if it is necessary to cover the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the cloth bandage.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the deep fistula
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodular and more numerous than those that come above the foundation, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or many; and when this nodulation is old, it works, and shortens moisture above white or subtle blood, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosities when the pain causes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that perforate the bladder, and perforate half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and perforate the anus.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the basement, and not passing: and it is that you press your thumb or base on the fistula, and thrust a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twist, then thrust a fine tent of lead, or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no piercing, egestion, or ventosity, as we have said: cut it so that it does not perforate; then hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent near the bladder or near the urethra, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated near the hip joint, then the tendon comes from the limb; if there is no twisting and the pain is internal, it is because it is dislocated, and there is no cure by medicine or ointment; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and vanity of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, in hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pains are hidden between your hands on his back; and the legs are raised up to his knees, and his knees are bent towards his belly; then pour a tin, or lead if there is twisting, until you remove the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you should insert your second finger, as if you are feeling for it; and if you feel between your thumb and index finger, then cut off what you find there; so do not struggle more than necessary to heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can heal almost anything, but this is rare; and the aid that is made, is to heat the cauterizing instrument according to the width of the fistula, as it was previously mentioned; and push it all the way into the fistula, until it comes out beyond the base; and do this two or three times, until you see that those sharp pieces are removed, which are similar to an arrowhead; then cure the wound with a burr, until those sharp pieces are removed, then cure the wound with ointment.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus sound, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If not, no other method can be sound; and if it is between the tent, and does not pierce just at the base where it is founded, and between your hand and the tent a thick covering of char or of syfac, and you see the fistula pointing to the covering of the cure; if the copper at the beginning of the fistula, and before the tent, and then the cauterization after it comes to the top of the tent; and he will be delivered from the tent, and chilled; then cleanse those char that seem like a quill of an eagle, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot remove it, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization assembles two things: to know, the burning of these charred parts, and the draining of blood and the scarring of moisture; then cure tents boiled in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as the wound does not gush blood, and if the charred parts are removed from the wound; then cure the wound with hard char, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from just above the base, and is distant from the body, then press on the top or base, and ask for water.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the cloth or thread or charcoal, where it is about to perforate, if there are no other means than faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods: whether you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut just above the base, or if you can put tents and cure as first; and do not move too much in front, that you do not cover the holding of the base, and bring the evacuations by the way of will; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it is cut below the base, or by tent or other appointed instrument; then remove the char that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to delay the fistula in the part before the base: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you push the tent into the fistula, it is where it costates on the foundation below the skin above, then take a tent perforated at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And push the thread into the fistula, and push the tent along the entire thread in the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is missing in the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread of that perforated one, so that you push your other or foundation; and take the head of the thread, and gather the two parts together, and hold them together, and let it stay for a day or two; and do not restrain it once, until the thread copes with those charred things that are between two, and heal; then cure the wound until it is dry and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then prick it in all possible ways that you can, but do not make it too thin.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not good to make the bandage too thin if it is too thin, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous spine that is made for the fistula should be very sharp and thin; on the one hand, it is partly sharp and cutting; on the other hand, not, because we do not want to do what we should not do, as you see here:
des emorroydes	des emorroydes
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	1. "Blisters occur in two ways: when they are within the foundation, like grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some have blood inside, and some have one or more, and some are under the foundation and at the base of the foundation; but those that are under have little moisture, and some have a little sharp citrine or a little blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the treatment of those who have them within the foundation is that you command the patient to urinate for other rooms, until the foundations are clean, and the child appears; then haste, and it can be held with pliers, or you hold it at your finger, then cover its roots; and if the hooks cannot hold because of their moisture, take them to a cloth, or a napkin, or a piece of cloth; then hold them in your hands, then cover, and powder with any hot powders that are in the cautery; or cauterize it as it is said in the chapter of cautery, because other cures treat it until it is healthy; and if the foundations cannot come out, wash the patient's mouth with a biting and rough paste to clean what is at the foundation, so that it can come out openly; then apply pressure, and if the blisters are large at the base of the foundation, it is a light treatment; and it is that you hold them at your finger or with pliers, then cover, and treat as we have said, until it is healthy, and does not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to mend the seam in this way: take a thread of twisted hair, and make it into a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and bring back the two ends of the thread on either side of the needle, and if it is too wide; and straighten the thread well, then remove the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to allow for the excess blood; then put under the foundation a linen cloth dipped in rose oil or cerot, and put under the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then let him rest until they are healed, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and without delay at the base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often occurs in the intestines and due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to scrape the surface with a spatula or your nail, which does not allow it to become moist; then treat it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be dried, then begin the scraping stronger than before until it is clean, and then treat it as it should be while it is clean.
dou fremit	dry heat
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Fumigation is a small appearance cut into the chest, and it goes up in front; and sometimes the true one finds the frost, and the smell is like that of dry heat, and it comes all over the body, and more in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the care is that you take a quill of a goose pen, or a pen of a vulture very strong, and put that quill on the wound, until the circle of the pen covers the wound all around; then return your hand to all the quill until you cover all around the wound, and put it in front, and remove the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then make a suture of a needle of rain or iron in this form, and be subtle to remove and raise it up:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	so that it does not pierce, to hold both sides and press; and if you see, then cauterize the wound, as it is before or chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of this ointment
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make an ointment of silver or lead, or melted tin or brass; and never make any of these small or large instruments according to those that you will arm yourself with.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those that you should arm yourself with in the care of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of this ointment is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a discharge or the belly is bound as you see, and the cloth is inside perforated; and at one of the sides it has two holes, and at the other one; and the belly or where one puts the medicines in a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is perforated all around with small holes, and between each hole there is one inch of space, then fill in these holes with a strong thread twisted in X or around, and tie up the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the cloth is attached to the instrument before by a strong thread, then ointment; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head of the poultice with oil or an egg yolk, or something similar, then press it gently; then the minister applies it to both hands together, until it is completely visible, then remove the poultice, and relieve the pain in his legs at the same time, and if the wound wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the poultice in the case of diarrhea, and the patient wants to come out, let him come out as much as possible; and if he is healthy again, continue.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	If the arrow is lodged in the foundation or abscess, it should be removed as carefully as possible for a child; and this is the form of the careful removal with which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	with wounds:
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said about the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to how they are made, and according to the limbs or wounds that are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing with a spear, and cutting of a sword or a lance, or a staff or an arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the limbs of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds to the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, take care if it is a piercing or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and is large, and you doubt lightly of an abscess: if you do this soon, heal the wound itself immediately if there is little blood from the wound, and heal the opposite part if necessary; and avoid the evils of overeating and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal, let him eat light food, and do not drink wine, and do not change his diet; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in sterile wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the wound has been moved, put on some ointments, as long as it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be closed by tents, then sew them together as I will say in wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and can be moved but holds only at one point, then bandage it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore a hard bandage in place of skin, and command the patient to eat soft foods, such as testicles and cooked grain, like chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have found leather or putrefaction and there is no bone, then bandage the whole of it with foul cloths, and then treat it; and if it has an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you have found it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should apply this powder that soothes as soon as the wound has been moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take a part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; live sulfur three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and joins together; then bind it firmly, and leave it undisturbed, unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never use only chalk, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the art has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the art has moved the wound immediately, then do not add this powder; but use some digestive ointments, or flour of oats made with honey and water, until it stops bleeding; then treat with other treatments until they are healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then strain it with fine needles; and I will tell you afterwards about the fractures of the main bone.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the previous one, but if the wound of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the neck, there is no other means than to leave the care, and do not put anything restricting, because it hurts the nerves and causes them to retract; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuity is with the brain, which is one of the highest members; but let the medicine be gentle, like salt washed in warm water, and mixed with rose oil, and the wound washed also in warm water, and other stones of this kind, and moist cloths.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then use bandages to bind it, and treat it until it heals.
