Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the bone is exposed and full of blood, then pierce or cut below the skin; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then suture it, and clean it, and cauterize it as necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the muscles, and the conductor is kept, by which the meat goes, then cut the tendon above the neck bone, and do not touch the neck but return it to its natural shape; and then gradually tighten, and leave it for some time, then treat the wounds of infection until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, try to remove them all, and if you cannot, leave them until the wound can heal and be aligned with the issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder over the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then the treatment as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of spear or of dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound of spear or dagger, and the wound is deep, look if from the wound there comes whitish pus that the hairs are not affected: cut then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in the first hour for the blood so that it does not coagulate in the wound, and return to the heart, and cover the pain; but put attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and make the pain sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor trembling of the heart from elsewhere; and when you see the good dispositions, cut that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of tents and other treatments, until they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, and work, then make an incision where there is a fistula; if the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an arrow or sword, and it is simple, or pierced in the front, back, or shoulder, then treat it as we have said; if it is large, stitch it; if it is small, apply powder, and if it has splinters inside the bone, and has broken pieces, remove them if they are removable; and if they are not removable, leave the wound to rot, so that the extractions will align; and for other wounds in other limbs, treat as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	abdominal hernia
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	abdominal hernias are large and medium and small; from the great wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines escape, by which the insertion of them; and the sewing is worse, and often the small wound is better than the big one, because one can more easily put back the intestines, if they are not put back immediately; because the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, if they are put back gently, and for this reason the medium-sized wound is better, because one can more easily sew up the intestine to its place as with other II And the tears of the abdomen are according to FOUR methods: the TWO common costures are in the costure of the abdomen, and the costure of the other wounds of the body and TWO other costures are common to other wounds; and all the same they are more proper with the costure of the abdomen, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the internal is injured, and it is easier to put back, it is done in one of the two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflated by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a handful of dry bread only with hot water, or cook it in hot squeaking and copper and spike, and roast the intestine until it is softened; and never do this restraining, and it is better to leave it to cool.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestines are moist from sharp or high and misshapen things, because by this means the entrance is soon made; and if it cannot enter, make a small opening with the instrument with which one removes impacted feces; and the first cure is to quiet the pain, that no one should cut without great necessity, and this is the tool for cutting: if you cut from within the belly and not outside, and remove the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, put them back in their natural form according to their own place, if you can, for this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part away from the belly, then you should place the injured part on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part away from the belly, then raise the head and the sore part higher than the other parts, and in such cases, manage as I have described for large and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply what is appropriate to the part, then place your hands between the wound and the skin, and use a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound, leaving one inch of space from the edge of the wound, and sew with a strong thread; pierce both layers of skin and flesh with the needle, until you have pierced through that part, and gather the two ends of the needle together; then wind the thread around the needle twice, and evenly sew the edges of the wound together, leaving one inch of space, and sew another stitch; tie the thread as you did with the first stitch, and do not stop doing this until the entire wound is sewn; and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cover the whole wound, and thick ones cannot enter well; for this reason, they should be medium-sized; and do not place the needles too far from the skin and flesh, so that they do not cut through the wound before sewing; then cover the edges of the needles with bandages or cloth to keep them in place, and let them stay until the wound is closed; this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires only one stitch; when you have pierced these edges together, remove the needle from the part where you started, in the manner of threading a needle; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a thumbnail; this method is used by tailors, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his abdomen, which was cut by a knife, and was more than an inch wide, and had intestines protruding two inches out, and the wound was inside the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed with a poultice after 15 hours, and it was treated, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine; and I poured water through the wound twice a day, and washed it with vinegar until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle, and the thread from the front part below; when it has perforated the curved part correctly in the middle, place the head of the needle on the side or stitch it where you have placed the thread, and make it perforate from the other side of the part below. The understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier makes the furs, and that you leave once the flesh of one part, and take it from another, until the sewing is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who gather the two parts together naturally and apply one of the main needles to the other head, in this way: stick a needle or main needle close to the wound, and make it pierce only that part alone, and leave the two wounds; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part inside, both wounds, then make it pierce one and the other from the front part inside, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common way of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	If one says this word, and no one testifies to it, then one should sew the belly with two needles, or one in each; and one should put one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corroies; and it is said that when the tear is in the belly, then the sewing is more painful than other sewings of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you clean the fresh wound completely with its blood, as soon as the art has moved it, then put back the intestine and the flesh; then put on powder mixed with charcoal, and if the art has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound closes; then bind the cloth, and be careful of the scar, and the mirror; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on cotton as soon as it begins to bleed, and shake it twenty times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For in other medical situations with many wound positions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with principal members, then it is necessary to apply a light oil of warm or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and wipe off the joints; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and often has, then clysterize with black wine, and immediately if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and perforate within, and scrape out whatever is inside, as when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is raw, and this is due to the smallness of the veins that are in it, and due to the subtlety of all the body, and its proximity to nerve nature.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, it must be put back as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned or blackened, then you must tie the part that is blackened, so that blood does not come into it, for there are veins and arteries in it; then cover what is between the limbs, and put the two ends hanging from the part outside of the wound, up to behind to help the extraction when the intestine dies, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breakage of the pot
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured, and the wound is small, if it can be restored to some men, because I saw that one man was pierced through the abdomen by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became an abscess and fistula, and in it there was egestion and ventosity; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to subtilize until he was healthy, and the others seemed good.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewn up, I doubted that the pains were not in his abdomen; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, it should be sewn up in this way: take a sharp knife, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the knife is over the mouth, put it across both lips so that it holds the mouth open; then cover the test with the other test, and hold it so that it cannot slip off, then use another sharp knife in this way as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief, if it burns inside the intestine, and no harm comes to the hairs, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the end of this intestine thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this thin thread, then wrap the thread around the needle, and pull the intestine, and reattach it at the tear; and this method of sewing is not far from the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no skill or health, because of its thinness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	all wounds or abscesses, when they are covered, are universally called "fistulas," and specifically when they are cut and opened up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the direction of the hard and white knots, where one does not feel pain, and it is also cut like a quill of an eagle; and sometimes it opens up clearly, and sometimes deeply; sometimes small, and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no discharge, except for one of the EIGHT causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or corruption; or because of its maliciousness; or because there is a hard discharge inside and on the lips, which does not let new discharge come out; or there is too much pus; or the wounds are poisoned, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is in the form of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late health, and flows by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistulas that are made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and from arteries, and from nerves, or to the face, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the main member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas that are of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to treat it, then take a lead or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, if the circle; and if the fistula is crooked, then use a thin tent of plaster, for the plasters stick to the twists; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot cover it well with tents, then cleanse one of the holes by pressing on it, because the moisture comes out from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then treat it carefully, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and if it is covered with a healthy flesh, and ask well of the patient about the pain he feels when you press on it, and where he feels it; and when you will know truly where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then treat it according to what I have told you, and remove the cause and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply set in the right place, then cut it open as much as you can, then put moist bandages in medicine ague, and press on the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous part that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments with clean cloth, until they are healed; and if they are not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves cause pain or harm to principal limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove all the corruption until it is completely gone, then treat the things injured with charms until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and remain as before, do not go any further: if it exposes and wants to be removed as much as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, do not go any further: there is no other remedy that is less harsh than nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can draw it out with pincers, then extract it with the appropriate tool, and if there are many bones, then take them all out, leaving none behind; and if the moisture makes it against you, and there is no error or fear, then use moisture and charms to deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something stinking on the wound to promote pus, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will be more easily broken; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, lift the corruption as far as possible from the bone, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption and comes to the surface of the bone; if the covenant so be, and cover all around the corruption, and then cure it until it is sound; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the chest, so that the matter came to the leg, and he was filled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open; but the physician by them opened so high that the abscesses opened, and they ran out of a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there was much pain that everyone groaned and moisture from the chest; and many more sought cure within two years, and there was no cure in the art of hands, so that I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was running through the fistulas was great; and he became red the chest of the young man, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that one was coming against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	Then I had to stop, and I cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and I found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from inside; I saw that what appeared to be rotten bone, and I thought there was no other corruption except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with various medicines for a long time, but I could not heal it; then I returned, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then I removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only cut around a palm's width of the bone, and I treated it all over its surface, then I returned it with medicines; and it became healthy and healed tightly, but it did not want to continue the work except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was completely healed, and born in the place of the bone, a hard char, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction at all, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take one ligature, and stretch it at the head of the bone that opens, and command it not to extend upwards; and put another ligature of thinner than the first ligature, and tie it above the char that is on the bone, and stretch the head, so that you remove the corrupted char from outside, and uncover the char above the place where you want it to be, so that it does not stick to the char; and put the tissue or a cloth outside the bone to cover the corrupted char; and it should be done as much as possible to see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is rotted and does not open, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, remove the tissue completely; then place a thread of silk from one part to the other, and sew the part where the corruption is, and let the silk be of the same length as the corruption, as we have said; and if the decay is in the joint, cover the joint with the rotted part, and sew the bone or the part that contains the other side; and if the decay is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other means than to cover it; and if the decay is at the tip of the finger or the toe, this is a very difficult thing, but nevertheless you must ask about this corrosion, how it opens; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or the nerve do anything against it; and know that the instruments for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason you must prepare an instrument for each kind of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you have to use, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument that you have to use according to what it should be.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints will rot due to causes within or without; and when you have treated the corruption with medicines, and it does not improve, then you must amputate the member up to the joint where the corruption comes from, so that the pains escape by death or by malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, so that they seem to be burned by fire, and then become blacker, as the corruption spreads from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body; if you hurry to amputate, and if the corruption is at the head of the toe, then amputate and do not give it time to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes from the hand, if the cloth is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cloth is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy but the quantity of its virtue; and thus do what you can when the corrosion comes: if it comes in the first joint, if the cloth after the other joint; and if it comes to the pain, if the cloth covers all the pain; and if it goes up the leg, if the cloth is at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to let the patient die of the pain; and the way of the cloth or the bandage is that you tie it over and outside, and extend some bandages on one side, and some bandages on the other side, and you scrape the char between the two bands to the width of a span, until the bone is exposed; then the cloth or bandage, and put a piece of linen on each part so that the cloth does not touch the healthy flesh, and it comes to the other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood flows when you are working, cauterize the wound hastily, or place some powders that stop the bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a black spot that seemed like fire burn, and that corrosion first appeared on his foot, spreading all over the foot; and when the doctor saw the corrosion, he covered the foot, and was healed; and after some time later the corrosion appeared again on the other foot, and it came to me, and I placed some things that reflect after cleansing the body's surface, and could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I would cut off his foot, and I did not want, because I had hope to reflect the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his foot, he would not die, for the virtue of the man was weak; and he gave up all hope, and returned to his land, and covered his foot, and was healed; and I have told you this only because it is necessary to do something else.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess ever forms in a wound that is not properly cleaned, and it may remain for such a long time that a great amount of pus accumulates; then it bursts and pierces, and the pus escapes, as if from a bag; and the skin above is as delicate as cloth, and does not stick to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinuses", and are not called "fistulas"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the outside, it is called a "fistula"; and the skin is such that you must cut around it, and even when it is delicate, as if it were cloth; and it does not heal due to its corruption.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from a small pouch beneath the finger, or the palm, or by chance in other places; and when it is opened, and no precaution is taken, if the abscess spreads, and corrodes and drips pus until it reaches the root of the finger, and perhaps corrodes it entirely; and then there are corrosions just above the bone, as long as there is painful putrefaction, and the affected area is red.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of verses that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow disease," because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes through the entire body, going up and down, and is felt by all members, as it goes to the skin where it wants to go, and jumps out; and it is caused by some humors, such as worms and lumbrics and ascarides or intestinal worms; and one doubts its malice, for as it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the oil, perhaps it enters, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that it needs to be cured and pulled out, you cannot do otherwise than when it goes: therefore it is necessary to hold the limb above and away from a very tightly closed wound, then cut across and pull it out, and if it turns out to be in front of the char, and you do not remove it, then cauterize with fire above, until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold it away from it firmly, then cut across, and pull it out; and it is necessary to use the remedy of healing with solutions of medicines for the harmful humors, and if it becomes swollen from eating spoiled food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "windiness", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a woman with pain, and I discovered that one of her arms was swollen, and I saw a small pustule in the armpit of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rise like a snake to the shoulder, faster than anything, as if alive when cutting into flesh; the pain departed from that arm, and went to the shoulder, and then it spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she turned around inside her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I greatly marveled at how it moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease move in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had heard that it could move from one limb to another, but I had never seen it do so, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and because that constraint appeared; and it did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease and the pain feels as we have said, if it appears to you as we have mentioned, then hold it above and below firmly, and then cut into it so that that constraint is released from the limb; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then treat the cause of those veins, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their similarities and according to the types of bodies they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are arrows with large points, and small ones, and hooked ones, and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those with tails, and those with pieces; and the one that pierces any member, depending on the manner: whether it pierces in the principal members such as the neck, brain, heart, spleen, lungs, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears: then it is necessary to extract this arrow, because death comes in many ways; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not completely removed, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the head when the arrow pierces and perforates the bone, and the syfac that is above the head, is blindness and dizziness and vomiting and blackout of the limbs, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without strength of the nose or the ears; and perhaps also the speech and voice; and a white discharge from the wound like pus, and also like boiling water; and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the patient, and remove the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The symptoms of a broken bone when it fractures or cracks, are that it is near the right breast, and also feels as if it were stuck in something hard, without being moved; and by chance the bone moves like a chicken's wing, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore, without doubt, the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that does not heal is that without any pain, bubbles rise from the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and it gasps for breath and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrowhead is stuck in the covering of the worst, it is between the small ribs; and it pours out much blood and great pain and breathlessness; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the stomach, by chance if anything of undigested meat jumps from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the belly, and nothing comes out of it through the intestines, there is no hope of cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bladder, and the urine comes out and goes away, and the pain is very great: it is certain that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the hand and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and spine of the back and forearm and wrist and fingers and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that hit him in the root of the nose: I tried to remove it, and took it out through another part beside the ear fat, and he was cured without much trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in one case, an arrow was stuck in the oil of the paper outside, and the arrow was removed, and it could only reach up to the tip facing the fist, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all the way to the light; the wound was cleaned, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And in one case, an arrow was stuck in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I cut off the barbs, and carefully removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And in one case, an arrow was stuck in a man, whether it was in the neck or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow, and twisted it, and removed it, and no bad accident occurred.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you want to heal a man who has an arrow stuck in him or his back, and the wound was sealed over; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor found harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you want to heal another man who had an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was sealed over; and it remained thus to suffer great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And if you remove an arrow from the man of princes, the king, who had it in his neck, and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely healed, I was called to cure after it had been for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied a thin needle to it and did not feel anything; and he felt no pricking or pain outside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of the arrow; I applied a digestive ointment to the wound because the wounds did not swell; and the arrows appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the ointment again later, and immediately healed the wound, and the pain lasted a long time until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound later, as long as it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which was inside; then I inserted it into the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the tip of the arrow appeared visibly; and it passed well through the ends in about four months, and then it extruded itself; therefore I did not cease to subtly and ingeniously contrive ways of instruments, until I got it one day with well-made forceps, according to how its form would come at the end of this chapter, so that I could remove and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeon judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and it was sewn up, and the injury was healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you might place your care on what I have not mentioned, for books cannot contain everything; but wise masters know many great things, and understand what is present and lacking, and find new work, and new instruments, in the removal of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the body in two ways: either by the way they enter, or by another part; and the one that issues by the way it entered, is an arrow entering into its own flesh, and has never issued before.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her remain until the charcoal is poured around her, and she is alleviated from the issue; and also if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot be removed, let her remain thus for several days, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, perforate all around with a fine needle, until the flesh around her is expanded, and then remove her.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the belly of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned above cause pain to the patient: if you do not remove it, but let it remain until it is even after several days, for if the arrow comes towards the face, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not embedded only in the bone, and does not come out of the skin, and remains in place without causing any harm for several days, then the method of pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be pulled out, then apply tar as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the flesh and cannot be seen, then apply tar to the whole tent; and if you feel it, then remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then leave it until the wound heals; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold it in place, then cut off the part that is deeply embedded and pull out the ears of the arrow, as much as you can, carefully so as not to break the arrow when removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, then pull the limb towards the shoulder, as the extraction is alleviated.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the wound makes you contrary, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put effort as you can pull the arrow without danger, or soon or late, or tightly or firmly; and put the pain according to the form it was when the arrow fell out, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place where we see or feel apart: cut then above, as much as the tongs can take, and then extract it: if it now breaks.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone, until it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then start the extraction again until it comes out; and if there is an arrow in the bone, and you see that it is stuck, and you administer gently, if you administer the instrument with a hair, so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then pull it out, and if the arrow is caught, pull the instrument in at the entrance to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces or sticks in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cut it out, do so; but do not cut into the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then treat the wound as appropriate; and treat until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the beak of a bird, to stick at the point of the arrow, as in this way:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the barbs to hook and to hold is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins that can be tapped from, of which there are 6 main ones, namely: 2 veins that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the 2 arteries that are in the temples apparent; and 2 veins that are in the arm pits of the arms, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the 2 jugulars that are on the neck; and the 2 veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and 2 veins that are outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly opened are five in each arm: the one is to the cephalic, and is on the right side, and is called by the people "the chief vein"; and the second is called "the forearm", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and is called by the people "the heart vein"; and the basilic is on the left side, and is called by the people "the belly vein", and is above the fossil, and is that which is opened, which opens manifestly above the bag.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the subclavian vein is the vein that is between the auricular and annular, and it is in the arm; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the first is outside the coronary of the right side; and the second is at the knee of the left costeit; and the vein which is called "the neck", which is at the knee of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The first line of the text appears to be discussing a medical procedure involving fire cauterization. The patient is instructed to allow their hairs to grow long and even, and if they feel any pricking at their base, they should hold their eyes steady so they do not move until the hairs have grown.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	For the healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is necessary to apply an ancient, wet, and ointmented cloth to them; and also to put the fingers of both hands across the eyes, and to press on the tear ducts at those places; and the quality of this treatment is as I said: and it is that the hairs strangely stand up, so that the two veins are clearly visible; and then you feel the pain in the eyelids, and then you gently lift the eyebrows above the vein on the outer side, and remove the lancet from there, and then lift the vein upwards, and cover it, as you did with the other two veins, and treat the blood according to your necessity; then remove the pain, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; then bandage it, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about its healing, its removal, and its extraction, at the beginning of this book.
