Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sound of the vein in the front of the neck is as valuable as the sound in the cephalic diseases of the face, and headaches, and rheumatism; and the qualities are such that the pains are strange in twisting the neck, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which is of this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see; then release the neck from the pain, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and never once with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not advisable that the flames be too strong; and the direction of the bone, for the bone is close, and by chance it may break the flames when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The direction of the two veins that are in the two armpits helps to those, and to the elbow, and to the wrist, and to the palm of the hand, and to diseases of the face; and the quality of their direction is such that the pain is strange when twisting from any part, as before; then the direction, and let the direction be across, a little long of the flame, a little wide, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, perhaps it will break; then apply blood clotting agents as you have skill, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vine's sap is good for ague and fever, and for diseases of the face, such as headaches and toothache that come in the face, and always when it is old; and the quality of the sap is that the pains tighten their neck, then strain their neck to your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it on the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well from there, and the blood will now begin to clot; and do not move too much at first, and apply blood clotting agents according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is soon restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	For the shoulder girdle, the application of a bandage helps to narrow the joint, and at the beginning of maltreatment, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosions, and in herpes, and in erysipelas; and the quality of the bandage is such that the pains are separated from one and the other, as we have said; and if the master is above the chief of the pain, and the pain sits on one seat, then apply the bandage around the long bone slightly wide, then draw out the blood promptly, or as much as the matter requires; then make another application on the other vein, then release the limb, and hold the veins steadily, that the pains do not entangle; and leave it just before morning, that the wound be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips above helps in the mouth, and in the corruption of teeth, and fissures of lips, and soreness and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the pain sit in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said; then return the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore match both, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, compare the largest of each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's disease
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The diseases of the veins that are outside the tongue help after the disease of the head, and it is by tightening the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is that the diseases stop between your hands in front of the sun, and the leaver the tongue, and look outside each side a black vein: therefore cure both, and do not move too much, for outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly cured are cured in two ways: either by pinching at all the flame miraculously wide, or by subtle pressure as if cutting through, and is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire cautery is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has skill to open veins that are closed and flat with large clotted blood visible, and that contain large clotted blood and disturbed; and this is the form of the fire cautery olive.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicate and pointed, and is for opening veins that are delicate, where there is delicate clotted blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and where the collarbone, and where the ribs, and where the abdomen; and it is important for the opener to open carefully, and to avoid the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, it is necessary to cool it, as I have said; and it should not be pricked with a flame, but cut off like an ear.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary to prick and change another one; or you want any blood from it, or you heal in its place the vein instead of the arm: it opens clearly; and cut off with the flame like we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the vein of the arm, it is also necessary to prick and hold the arm until you touch the vein; then sign the vein with your finger, and then bind the arm, and cut off the vein with the flame like we have said; and beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it coming out high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, it is from an artery: then hurry, and put your hand long on it, then remove your hand without stopping, as it often does; hold the arm, and let it be still, and do not move the painful part; and be in fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the blood is not stopped, and you feel it, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the main part retreats; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a small splint, and make it, and take one of the halves and fasten it well to the other side; if it is not stained, it is good; if not, then the cure, as we have said, with the powders that stop bleeding; and the staining does not last in many positions for the small part of the wound, and the position of the bone of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle helps to treat blood by treating it above the chief and the body, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and the saint should be for all the nerve that is out, and if not too much in front, and he finds the nerve, and he inflates and it is stained, and perhaps cannot be healed; and this nerve opens often, and if it does not open in any man by its subtlety, then you should saint the nerve with the instrument and remove the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has veins between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The salve of the cephalic, if it draws blood from the head, and helps in the veins; and it is necessary to apply the salve by pricking with an olive or a thorn, because it is the safest of all the veins, as it does not have any nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the lightest vein, and not to cause any harm if one must do it the first time, and then start again; and sometimes the veins swell in some people, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that healing is only intended to maintain health and prevent diseases from coming; and the healing should be done in one of the three veins that are located: namely, cephalic, fascia, and basilic; and if it should be done at the beginning of the first hour or third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healing given for diseases has no determined time, but it is necessary to do it every hour and at all times; and it is not necessary to heal children under the age of fourteen, nor pregnant women except during the first three months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not let those who have passed sixty years old become physicians.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When someone wants to become a physician in any way, it is necessary for him to examine the intestines of a light chyme if he has much feces retained, so that the veins do not attract excess and harmful substances to the principal members; and one should not become a physician if he is too healthy from meats, or fat, or watery; and if he has had colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent traveling, watching, and fasting, and all the virtue of the body or arm; then subtly the humors, without being too heavy, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then enter or bathe, if nothing prevents, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the vein in the middle of the third hour, as we have said; and guard him that day from work, from pain, from pleasure, and similar things; and be careful and joyful, and let the physician be higher than those who are sick, and let the one who fetches the hand rub it twice or three times, then stretch the joint above the middle movement, because when it is too stiff or weak, it cannot correct itself; and then rub the hand with the main hand until the veins swell, and feel on; then wipe the physician's flame with a small amount of old oil, then put his right hand on top of the vein of the hand where he wants to suck, that the vein does not fail to strike.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as if by strings to the barber, and there are some that are plain from their softness, such that when one puts on the flame, they retract from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if the barber opens the vein, if the wound is too tight, because it is necessary that the barber be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, one should try again a little below that place or above, until the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed, and the pain spreads, let him rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will come; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the skin is cut subtly and you doubt that there is as much blood as you saw, then trust in that wound alone to the direct flame; and work a little hastily, also as long as the veins are inflamed; for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swelling, do not begin again with the same salve, and put on a little oil, for it reduces the flow of blood, and is healing in this limb like the oil; and thus administer the oil in every salve that you use to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing applies to triangular and bandage dressings, when it is put on the limb; and gently remove the swelling and separate it when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there are large abscesses that often occur, exactly when it is not healed except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, you hurry, and put on the limb soft sponge in hot water and a little cloth, and hold it for an hour; and it should be done after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for any days without any black or greenish discoloration, do not remove it; and if you see, put on anything of aloe or of mercury mixed in juice of camomile, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the base of the church: place your hand over it, and if you press too hard with your hand, that is the wrong appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not place anything that we have said above on it, for perhaps you will cut the artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the wound, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And apply each bleeding according to the amount of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the bleeding is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for those who are strong and able, and have the task of arrow extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and frequently bandage them, and it is best to bandage by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of bandaging is safe from infection and nerve compression, and is better than long or wide wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose body needs bandaging, it is appropriate to give bread soaked in juice of green apples; if they are hot-blooded, take out the arrow three times or four times, and if they are cold-blooded, before bandaging, give bread soaked in honey syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and strongly scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he has a fever after the evacuation of much blood, it is necessary to give him a broth of meat, and an odorous syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the chapter or section on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to drain some arm and bleed again, it is necessary that when he is weakened by much bleeding, he should do so little by little, according to the quantity of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wishes to drain some arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong pulse, he should bleed again seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And those who wish to heal on another side, they must heal at the second hour or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood within the body that is already heated, and causes fever; if one must draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bleeds freely; then one must fulfill all the conditions of healing, and place one's hand on the wound when it is healed, so that the patient does not die in the absence of bloodletting, and this has often happened, when the healer is negligent; and it is not necessary to press firmly on the second arm, and draw out blood again, and the vein is closed, but if it is twisted, extend the arm quickly, for this would be harmful; but let it bleed until it is healed the second time; or you are at the tip of the flame, so that the blood frozen in the vein issues freely, and put a small piece of cloth on it to cool it, and press firmly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the pus is seen to be flowing, let it flow and do not press it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood the second time, draw it from the same vein, or another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are sound because they are composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of drawing blood is that the hairs bend their hand in hot water, until the veins are red; then tie it loosely, so that the vein appears well, then draw blood through the cross, not too wide or too long; and let the punctures be large, and draw blood well near the joint of the hand, and if none can issue, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the hot, until you have enough; and if it is in this state, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it puts more into shock than before; and drawing blood from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the savior of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how: strain the hand, and boil in hot water until the vein is emptied, if one can see it; and if the salve is against the grain, and if you apply it with everything, it will not hurt anything; and do not leave it too long, for the nerves are all exposed to the char, and then put the hand in hot water, if the wound is not frozen, and it cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary, if you put oil and thread over the vein to sew quickly, and thus do for each rain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the hand on the right side is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you to the left.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve for the breast is good for all diseases that are not of the body, such as diseases of the marsh, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rain, and of the coxes and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its salve is that the diseases are boiled in hot water, and rubbed on the vein until it perishes, and tied above the joint; and the vein is at the elbow, and by above the knee goes much rain; therefore the salve is good for a large vein, or at the elbow, that moves.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have the healthy above the knee, and you are warned of the nerves that are dislocated, and the sinew crosses as in copulating; and let the flames be equal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the sinew, then reset the knee in the high position, and let the vein fully drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sinew must be started first, then start the second above a little, for the legs are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make the other sinew evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the knee of the thigh, and its sinew is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for an arrow wound.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sweat is such that the hairs between or bath, and it strangles above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and across; and it is good to cover it, for the feet are clean, and it is very often done by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not straighten it, then it heals no wound of those who open or close the door to the small dog, and stays with the nerves; and correct so much blood that you see, and then release the tendon, and put it on cotton and hold it tight; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wounds by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction wounds are made of needles, or of iron, or of glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways: either all at once, or gradually; and suction made by pricking and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body, of which one is entirely on the chest; and the others are moved to the neck; and the other two are in the two shoulders; and the suction below the chin; and the suction on the two arms; and the suction on the two legs; and the suction on the two ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, but only small veins that are scattered throughout the body, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with bloodletting; and it should not be administered, neither at all heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of diseases requires ventosing, or by habit, one should perform it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each turn; for there are some who, when they have to undergo ventosing, feel heavy; and there are some who experience swelling and redness in their face, and on their head, and in their eyes; and there are some who taste a drop of blood in their mouth, and spit it out, and reach for the blood; and there are some who snore, and see through sputum and dripping and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is at the end of the month, we command them to fast for three hours after midday.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The cleansing of the mouth aids in the healing of the head … that comes to them, and it is only necessary after the evacuation of all the blood; and this fasting is in place of the cleansing of the cephalic, and it is only necessary for those who are of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, because this does great harm; and for this reason it is not necessary for the guardians to use it, nor for those who have or cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves, if they become forgetful, and for this reason, it is necessary to place the vacuum a little lower due to the uncertainty of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The vacuum is placed on the neck in place of the head and the basin, and for this reason, it is necessary to have it at the narrowest point, and to bend the channel of the pormon, and to all, and to replenish; and it should be placed a little loosely, because if it holds too tightly, it may cause forgetfulness or stomach pain and other problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The vacuum on the two ribs of the neck is useful for head pain, and obtunding, and emigraining, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the healing of the basin; and it is necessary to command the healer to put his hand when placing it, that he does not press the artery, and does not cause blood to flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventilation of the mouth should be done for diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation of the elbows is as much as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and commands the healer that he does not pierce too deeply in front, for the inside is bare of flesh, and knows of nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back should be used for emerging diseases from the foundation, and for diseases of dislocation, and it should be a large and made of metal, that it can properly pull; and by chance, if it is too thin, it will break; and I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups heal openly, because they attract blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the rain, and of the marsh, and of the bladder, and remove the sores; and they are in place of the two shins, and the two knees, and everywhere they weaken the body after long use, and bring on paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is that you first place it empty and then quickly suck out the air, press it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the flesh turn red and swell, and the blood appears; then stop, and remove the cupping glasses, and take care of the wounds, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: if necessary, it is best to strike once only, and it is best to make wide wounds, and a few deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the skin is thick, it is best to strike twice: the first time to make a more subtle path for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very sharp, you must strike it a third time; and when we want to draw out the arrow slightly and slowly, we should only pull once with great skill.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to draw out much blood, we recommend often; and if the bone is sharp, we should strike it in front, and the end should be perceived firmly, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are strong, and who have sharp pores, that you use the tips of oil vacuums appetizing and dissolving: if it is in this state, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of pennyroyal oil, or of lily, or of camomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balm oil, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if that person who is to have a wide and large opening, should not put any oil, but it should be washed after venting with hot rosewater, or hot cold water, or water of elderflower, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from the ashes of silphium, or hot water of mint, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive flesh rise from old wine, or vinegar, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be purged immediately before bathing or in the bath, but an hour or two after bathing; and they should not sleep immediately after ventosation, and it is best for them to move around when they should be ventosed and when they are being ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are purged are choleric, and if they are not too much agitated and inflamed; then it is best for them to take cold things, such as large apples and endives and lettuces in sauce, and similar things; and broths with pumpkin and char of Castile, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold constitution should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine that is between old and new, and a little mustard, and little pinch of pepper and small birds; and on the day they will be venturing, they should drink more than they usually do; and it is necessary to give some men once triphala or muscat before the venturing, or after, to strengthen the main members; and the subtleties should not be given to everyone, but only those who are cold-blooded.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the body are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and podagra, and on the stomach and buttocks and the thighs and the hip, because these members do not suffer much from suction on the outside, and no one does it except to draw blood from one member to another, as we put suction cups on the breast when the newborn is sick; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the stomach and buttocks to soften the member; and it removes pain, when there is an abscess or stone, if by its attractive power it happens to remove the abscess, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it is done when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for sweat alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with cold water, as in diseases of high fever, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot or cold water where it has cooked harmful herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the pneumatic administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two inches of width and half a palm in length, and has or costitals around the middle one small hole, as to put an needle, and it is of brass, lead before so that it does not burn the hair when putting it on the limb; and it has in the middle a rod of brass or iron, for putting a wick gripped, and there are large and small according to diseases and age of those who take them; for the vacuums of children are other than of old, and thin than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this suction cup on the limb: take the wax or liniment, and put it inside the suction cup at the end of the rod that is in the suction cup, so that the light may be at the bottom of the suction cup and not burn the hairs; then place it on the limb, and do so as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor comes out, and remove the suction cup; and take the liniment as before, and start again often, if you have the opportunity.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	Therefore, in the suction cup that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all times, there is no rod or stopper, and it is not administered until it is full of vapor, and it is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without sutures are only used in members where one cannot place adhesive strips due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in those that are bare, such as two or nostrils, and others similar; and the quality of using them is that when you remove sutures that are in soft water without pressure, take them; and put them in soft water until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then wash with blood and adhesive strips, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sutures; and when they are flat, and dry, if it is a place where one can place adhesive strips, place them, for this is very useful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the limb from the elbow, and then from the shoulder, very well, and then wipe it; and if the wound is too large after the furrows of the sinews, then dampen a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the sinews are cleansed; and if the sinews multiply, then put on broken glass, or salves, and similar things, until they are cleansed; or you put half of pounded beans on the wound, and let them remain until they burn the limb, then it will stop bleeding; and if you have more, then take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the snakes do not want to take, rub the flesh of blood fresh, or you put a needle so that the snake bites, and then put them above, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will die; and when you see that they are dying, powder with a little aloe and ground silk, or ash, they will now bleed.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Be careful, dear child, that the foolish ones do not see this chapter, as they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they read any; and for this reason the science is unknown in our land, because I have never found any good one; and I know nothing, except by the knowledge of the ancient books that I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are brought about, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and delay over the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or wounding comes to any part, it is necessary that you hasten to clean the wound on both sides, if nothing prevents, as weakness of body, or children, or old people; or if the joint is not very loose, or too stiff; and use cold compresses, that is to say, cold joutes, and eye and chicken broth, and do not drink wine, and do not use any heavy meats, and do not overfill your stomach with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of abscess, or spread of matter to the member; if the wounds return to their previous governance as they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a moistening remedy that causes swelling, such as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and beans, and piez, and fish, and wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the moistening remedy may cause pain and more quickly the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the elderly and infirm cannot be well mended or soldered according to their nature due to the corruption of the members, neither thus those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but rather, reset the broken bone above the joint, and join the member together, until it is strong again; and do not leave it entirely without work, and for this reason, it is necessary to apply a moistening remedy of large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And there are various ways to break bones in many different manners.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breaking of the shoulder is different from the breaking of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes through the arm, and another in soaking, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break all in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each manner there is its own method, and proper tool in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place; and the break of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and open well by default, and it is at the pressing of the hand; and when there is no twistiness nor touching, and the pains are not great, if there is no break; but it can still have twistiness, or cut, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it by hand, but put on the remedies that come after, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the fracture that was in pieces, and the two parts are disjointed, you should now put them evenly together, as soon as the swelling comes; and if the swelling is hard and painful, do not move it until the swelling is eased; then gently place it in a position where you can easily and safely move it, and if the restoration of the limb is lighter than the restoration of that where there are pieces, then hold it now as after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, it should be set in two parts, whether by hand or by a splint, or by a bandage at your discretion; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken bone are healed, you should gradually remove the additions in their places with care, and guard that through your work no further injury or pain comes; and properly set the two broken bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if you think it is not quite right: if it is well-dressed, and do not strain it too much, nor press it as those who bring their own cures for abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at a point, carefully restrain the painful part so it does not move, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way; and ensure that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet at a point, and you should put it in the correct position so it feels no pain; and ensure that it is placed straightly, that twisting does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the member broken is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The qualities of the member broken are different in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: if they are thin, cover them with soft linen cloths; and those that are thick, such as thighs and calves: if they are thick, cover them with a wide and strong cloth, for the wide cloths embrace the whole member evenly, and hold it equally in all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap light dressings around the limb, three or four times depending on the length of the limb, and hold your hand at the edge of the wound, then move up a little above the wound and hold it less, as the wound moves away from the edge; and gradually soften the cloth until you feel a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another cloth and return around the injured limb; then go to the part away from the wound, and hold it gently, not too hard or too painfully, as we have said in the first part above; then put between the cloths linen or cloth dressings, until they are all even, then tie everything together from above with a bandage, and then put your well-made bandages on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or boil, put something soothing on it, and what opens the abscess, and leave it like that for some time; then strain it through a fine cloth, or a reed used to make clips, or a palm leaf, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the thread that one puts on the break should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as it needs for the limb of small or large size; then strain it through the threads as you did in the first layer, then tie it up again, as you did in the first layer above the break; the tighter it is, the less; and it should be a medium thread, not too thick or too thin, and it should be made of linen; for if the thread is too thick, like the works of the folk who make the threads of the laces of the linen strings twisted, and this is great error, because the layer cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should only have at least two spaces between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the needles of the stitches after straightening them in their places, put some discharge of linen or other clean cloth, so that it does not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splint, and the bandages are broken, I will tell you the treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is not necessary to straighten all the broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put stitches for at least five days or seven, or more depending on the risk of abscess; and here is the manner of the ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and you should take flour that is kept in a mill wall, and mix it with enough egg, and use this mixture, not too clear or too thick, and apply it, and this is the common method of the restoring plaster for many positions, and especially for women and small children, because it is not too hard or too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations and twists: take aloe wood and ladanum and enulae and asafetida and Arabic gum and myrrh, in equal parts; wormwood and aloes, in equal parts; achillea, in equal parts; and make a powder, and mix it with honey; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it restores broken bones quickly, and it is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is good for twists: take myrrh and valerian, in equal parts; wormwood and aloes, in equal parts; achillea, in equal parts; Arabic gum, in equal parts; and grind it well, and mix it with vinegar or honey, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat joints and bones that have been dislocated or broken, to ease the pain, and to use the bone as a splint, and the fracture: take a new cloth, and moisten it in hot oil, and place it on the injured area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These bandages do not heal immediately, but they are good for easing abscesses and properly treating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat broken bones that heals: take dried fig leaves and earthworms, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat the healing of broken bones and to ease the remaining pain of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of wormwood, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one in parts; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are chilled, mix with a mustard plaster, moist or dry, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying the plaster more strongly than the first, when an abscess is resistant to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the root of wormwood, linseed, balm, melilot, and sanicule, and flowers of violets and camomile, of each one in parts; and grind, and mix with mustard salt, or sweet mustard, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it, for the reason that a cerote made of wax and oil was used, and nothing else, and he said that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, with dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat an injury and pain: take the feathers of a peacock or the quills of a porcupine, and mix them with honey and salt, and apply the mixture evenly on the wound and the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then relieve the joint after a while, and be careful if the hairs do not feel any pain, nor have they moved the bone of its place; then do not relieve by force later. And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or inflammation, then hurry, and relieve it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light bandage, and moisten with sea water, and soak in hot, and lift the limb, until the itching stops, and the pain is eased; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry cloth, moistened in hot or rose oil, and tie with a nut, as long as you are sure of no abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and it is eased of pain, then restart the thin poultice, and a little poultice, and do not strain it as much as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is filled with pus and redness and pain and swelling, and you have the skill of plastering and bandaging, then treat it evenly as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.
