If it does not come to the limb as we have said within three days or four or five or seven, and you leave it for twenty days, until the bone heals, and approaches the joint above; then tighten it more than before, and increase its flesh, as I have said before. And if you see that the limb is too hard, then soak it in hot water every time you dislocate it, and this should be done every day, and slacken the ligament a little; by this method, you will prevent the bone from healing crookedly: this is bad, and if such methods are painful, I see no other choice than to treat it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are various methods of breaking, and different figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collar bone completely breaks the bone just above the face which is outside the bone, as if it were broken or fractured; and because of this, this method of breakage is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above, perforating it, and this method of breakage is called «absolute»; and it is the wound of these two breaks, large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion from above, or a cut or from the fall of a stone, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a broken bone that protrudes, which approaches the skin that is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is set in the bone as subtle as a thorn, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound that is made by being hit by an arrow, or by falling, or by something similar, and allows the piece of the bone to enter below, and the threads are like those of a hat when they are nailed on the hat; then the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are those who have more under them that are either wet or dry bones, such as the head of a child; and they have all these ways of fracture where small pieces are broken off like these; and I will speak to you about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of fractures by the withdrawal above them, and inquiry with tenting, and by the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when the bone is exposed and rubbed with something, if there is an open fracture, it is black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, beware of bad accidents, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes coming out and reddening, and other similar things in many conditions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any obvious injury, and you hope for healing, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone comes first to you, and it is in the leg, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day, so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the arm, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the skin around the bone is not decayed, and the injuries that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then you must cut away the part that is broken in such a way: and you must hold the head of the painful wound, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and over the figure of the wound more softly than you can, and if blood comes to reveal the bone, or an abscess forms, then help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with moist cloths in red oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is soothed, and make sure that the blood does not flow; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to the two methods of work: one method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many cutting instruments of different sizes, some sharp and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is very hard and out of position, it is necessary that you perforate around it, as long as you administer cutting instruments with trephines, not to penetrate beyond the jawbone, and it should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each time it comes in its own position of the body of the tooth, so that you have trephines for all teeth; and this is the form of the three methods of trephining.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for puncturing around the broken bone are that you place the needle on top of the bone, and return to your left until you feel that the bone is punctured; then remove the needle slightly after, and do so all around, then cover the incisions with the space between the teeth, and do this as delicately as possible, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as pliers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have punctured and treated the bone, it is advisable to close the opening that remains on the other side of the bone, similar to an incision, but it must be more flexible and more delicate than the other incision; and if there remain any small bones or scales, remove them gently with the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which the Galienics call, which is more safe; and it is very good, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must remove a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you can insert the lens-shaped piece of this surgical instrument into it:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the fractured piece is in two parts, so that the cutter is against the bone; then firmly strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, lightly cut the bone, because it is cut well without causing harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone's fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only broken from above, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth out that roughness, and remove the scales with the delicate scraper that you should have various quantities of, to manage each limb according to its convenience, following the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use great scrapers first, and then more delicate ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair and fracture files, you should manage according to its convenience; and this is a thing that is not returned to the one who put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so as not to aggravate the wound, then administer by pouring over another liquid, and do not restrain it except until the wound is healed; and leave it in this way for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder and place it on the wound, and administer moist medicines without biting; and keep the wound clean, do not leave any dressing, because when bandages gather on the brain cloth, it corrodes and causes great harm; for when something sharp is placed on the wound, it does not heal.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take precaution then, for if no accidents come to the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no other harm comes to the patient except what has been put on by medicine, which has its virtue, then it is necessary that you apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one cloth, and place it on the wound; then cure in ways of curing that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	It is said that the two bones above the nose are never broken, or one at a time, for they are cartilaginous and do not break easily, unless there is an injury or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you beat your small nail or needle through the break in your index finger, and place it inside the break, and at the pouch by default, until the bone regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and guard that the pain does not feel through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nail, and cannot reach the finger to the bone, then it is necessary that you place it inside the head of a pin or needle, slightly larger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, then make another, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the wound is calmed, then beat at the head of the nail with linen cloths, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you place it on the other side, if the fracture is there; and the tents are so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no restorer should moisten the tents in the morning, and kill each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think this is correct, but it should be moistened with an ointment of honey and powdered myrrh; then leave the tent until the bone is healed, and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use feather pens in place of tents, and if the sore is covered with a linen cloth, and the fracture is held, and blows the pain away; then do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, put cotton or milled cloth soaked in red oil or a drop of iodine into it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come to the nose, apply a poultice of crushed wormwood flour and powdered incense, mixed with a little honey, then place light cloths on it and do not bind tightly around the nose; if the broken piece of the nose is small and in many pieces, remove them with suitable instruments, then cut the wound, and the care of things in the meantime char, and seal, as suitable emplastrums and ointments for the nose; and if there is no wound inside the nose, apply bandages and place hot water bottles on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured, and there is no wound elsewhere, and the fracture is only slight, and not completely broken into two pieces, because of the teeth inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the lower part, to push your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, push your right index finger from the right hand, and push the fracture inside lightly, and hold it with the other hand by default, and make even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is in two parts, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth avails, or breakage, then strain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken mandible, and put on a double cloth; and put on the cloth a great strong stele well made, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it to the muscles that you can, and command the patient not to move, and give him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, then let it rest with the animal for a day, and then put it back to its original position; and apply a poultice on top, made of flour from the mill mixed with abundant urine or wheat flour, after you have removed the crust; and apply another light poultice on top of that, if the poultice becomes hard, leave it until it is healed; often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come to the face, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, treat it by not removing any piece of the bone that is broken; but gradually remove the bone with small instruments to the place where it should be.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then expand it according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have removed all these pieces, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, and it has been cleaned, then apply ointments to it, to draw out pus until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the bandage
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The bandage is broken several times against, behind the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways: either it is broken and torn into two, and there are pieces, and it is the least heavy to restore; or there is a breakage with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the fracture is near the wound, you should have two ministers, one to tend to the injury where the broken bone is; and the other to extend the neck towards the affected part; then place the fracture equal to your fingers, so that it forms as it should be, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round, soft cloth or linen ball on the shoulder, as large as your need; extend and lift the broken bone, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you can place it equal to the fracture, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the shoulder of the arm from behind, because it comes out in front, then it is necessary that the hairs of the armpit be pulled evenly over their surface, and the assistant holds the shoulder back, and pushes the shoulder down, until the bone of the arm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then approach the fracture with your fingers, and if you find broken pieces, it is necessary that you cut through; and gently pick up the pieces, and if the bones cannot join for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have; but place the instrument away from the arm, to guard against the splinter:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It resembles a spoon, and is not fixed in place, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and it has two prongs, as you see, and one is wide and the other narrow, like the edge of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of an abscess, if the wound is large, or you doubt an abscess, if the wound is small, then use the dressing and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if it is an abscess that comes, then soak the bandage in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The application of the bone, whether it is in pain or not, is that you place the plaster of the mill powder and some flour on top of the bone, and place light bandages on it, and place a ball outside the joint, if you have the skill; then take a very large bandage of one palm wide and long, and double the bandage over the bandages and the plaster; then take a thin strip of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the large bandage so that the head of the large bandage is suspended; and place the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the neck, and remove the ball outside the joint, and remove the ball from the bad part; and bandage each part, and when you see that the limb holds the fracture evenly, and you clearly see that the strip does not move over the broken bone, reward every day, and when the limb is healed, restrain it; place the bad part on its back, and put a small bandage outside the joint to lift the fracture high; align the fracture by the alignment of the shoulder, or you fasten the arm to the collarbone, and do not remove the bandage unless there is a bad accident, for up to 20 days; then restart the plaster, if you see that it has healed, and strain and leave it until it is restored; it is restored in the most 28 days, and less to some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder is broken or dislocated from its joint, and it does not move except by touch; then according to the figure of the fracture, and the bone is reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put powder from the mill with abundance of salt on the limb, and apply light dressings, and put over a double cloth; then put on a wide and delicate splint, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if the splint does not touch any part of the shoulder, then use a piece of linen to evenly cover it; and then firmly bandage all around, so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch the limb every day; and every time it breaks, again bandage, and make sure the splint is evenly placed on the side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days, and when this number is completed, then remove it, and be careful, for this is not bone that heals quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is sticking out before, and not completely outside, then cut it off, and the bone, and do as we have said in the fracture of the forearm to alleviate an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the pinky
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The pinky is never broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the base.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends outwards, and the patient feels great pain, and loss of all function, and possibly vomiting blood, and open the veins in the broken bone, and the patient feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the hairs are gently pulled upwards from their base, and the medicine is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades, and assemble the ribs of both ribcages in your hands, and subtly place them evenly in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place salves and dressings above the thinnest part of the bone, or another light one, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so it does not move; and return the limb gently to the back, and slowly extend it, and rewrap the bandage every hour, and if it moves, repeat the extension; and if it needs to be slid off for corrosion or for itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and remove it, and clean the salve, and address what has come from methods of healing; then reapply the salve, and extend it as long as it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	that the rib fracture only occurs after heavy blows to the back and at the base of the neck, and only if they are sharp; and the patient feels it well during the examination as we have seen.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and the bandage with a splint if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is declining inwards, it causes great pain and tenderness, like pleurisy, because the ribs do not touch the cloth; and it must be drained, and everything and a lot of blood, and it is a very bad sickness, and the ancients have used great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it should be administered foods that cause the stomach to swell, to push the broken bone out of place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	Let us not do this, unless there is a case where it does not come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of those who put suction cups on the limb for good drainage, and this is reasonable; however, doubt arises because the suction cup does not draw the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of those who should cover the limb with wool smeared in oil high, and put tents between the ribs to equal the liquid inside, then heal the care of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that it cannot be borne by the bone that does not cover it, and there is doubt, then one must cut across the broken rib on the side, and one must place a splint to hold the wound open; and then one must break the bone, and gently pull it out, and then suture the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with ointments, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess appears on the skin, place moist cloths soaked in red oil on it, and cover it; and treat the affected area as needed for the abscess, and let it lie quietly near the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when the breaker breaks the bones of the neck, and hardly ever does it rain; and likewise at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you see whether they will be healthy or not, if you take note if their hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is often fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you hold them and not, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the pains are healed, if you put care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you know whether it is healthy or not, if you take warning if the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and on top of the back, there is ventosity and egestion without will; and when they lie on their belly, there is egestion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it lies on its back and wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is a fatal condition: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, it is the lighter of the two.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the care is that you reward if there is an abscess, to put on the back rose oil or goose fat, as long as it is calmed; then put on one of the healing and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where you feel the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone dries, it is necessary to cover it with the care; then take the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, at a seam, then treat the ointment infusing charcoal, as long as it is healed; and if the patient’s bones are broken, which is called the “bone of the cow”, if you have a pouch in your right hand, and put it evenly on the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the splint on top, if you have the skill; then tighten it, and if there is a bone that has dried again, do it again, and take the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It is rare that the ribs of the back are broken, and if they are, it does not matter much to the head; and when it is long, and declines to the parched, and comes to the bad pain to the limb, and pointure, and swelling as what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, until you are over the broken part; and cut away those that are the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the top, then set it evenly until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long and it declines inwards, place the limb above its belly until the restoration of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it evenly, place the plaster on top, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fractured part still so it does not move; and fill the limb with wool until it is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their sound side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and place on top of what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and hold as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is located between the neck and the top of the shoulder. If it is fractured, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: the first method is that you take a piece of smooth wood, in the following form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two pieces together, and lift them up, and saw the broken part above the seat; then pour some brine on the broken piece until it becomes loose, and put a hook of wood in it, then lift any heavy object or the assistant extends it downwards; then place the broken parts together in his hands, so that the broken person returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one pricks the sore above its base, and places the hand on his collar, then commands two ministers to prick the vein that is above the breaker at his hands, and the others prick everywhere around it, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the eye away from the breaker, above the breaker, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breaker is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary to place the middle line away from the acromion, and the other towards the back, away from the breaker; and similarly, if the breaker is towards the back, then it is necessary to place the line lightly, without labor, until the breaker is even above the shoulder, and above the back; then equalize the fracture, as it should be, and stretch it, if there are no signs of apostem.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes, do not hold it for more than seven days, and put milk and rose oil on it until the abscess is soothed; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you place the plaster on the breaking part, then assemble the arm above the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and hold it above the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and put a wider and stronger splint than the others on the break, and have between each splint two fingers' width, and let each splint be so large that it passes the break three fingers from each side; then hold above the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, more firmly and less far away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the stones, and the traction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is healed, let it rest for seven days, as we have said; then look at the joint every three hours, that the wound does not swell or inflame, or the pus does not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come, let the dislocation wait for three hours or more, and let the pain lie on its back, and have its hands on its stomach; and put out of the aid a clean cloth equally, and look at every hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken member does not move, or the joints are not softened; if the direction is by the virtue of medicine, and give it the food we have previously given, in such a way that the food is very thin; and when it begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in forty days after everything; and then one must remove and administer a bath and medicines of ointments for the limb to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If its structure is crooked and swollen, it may take forty days or two months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus" and the "radius", one of which is small and is the one that forms the elbow; and the other is large and is the one that is outside, towards the little finger; perhaps the great humerus alone is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light and the healing; and when the large bones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If the small bones are broken alone, then it is best to slightly extend and align them.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if the large bones are broken, then it is best to stretch them more forcefully; and extend over the cushion, and tie the palm of the hand higher than the other fingers, and the small fingers lower than the others, and so that the hairs cross over themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the hairs do not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers to the part outside his hand, or to the elbow, and other ministers above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no need to hold the bone in place, and you cannot restore it to its original position, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken piece there is a wound, I have spoken about it to the chapter of the chaplain; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, then glue the cloth of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, which is not too soft or too hard; and bind the cloth subtly, until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then, remove the crust, and apply the poultice of flour from the mill with abundant urine, then place the splints, and set the broken one slightly further out and a bit wider than the others; and it should have six splints or more in various positions: whether the breaker is in one of the bones, or in two; and it should be held higher than the breaker than any other part, and always less distant, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are over the breaker be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the member and the limb after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any evil accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must raise the member in hot water, until the itching is soothed; and let the member rest loosely.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then continue the strapping, and if the joint is dislocated and the bones are displaced, similarly, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tendons cannot come to the member, because it is too tight, then you must slacken it slightly, and let it rest for some time, until the tendons are corrected, and then strap it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have said come to harm, it will not be necessary to look at them for twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Then let the hands be placed on his neck, and make his neck even, and keep him still and quiet, and sleep on his back; and if this broken bone is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breakage of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Then let it be at the back of the hand and we have few breakages, and only bleeding many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plantar bone of the hand is broken or crushed, it is necessary that the hairs be cut straight and evenly; then place the hand on the extended palm, and extend the surgeon's fingers over the broken bones, and place them evenly together until they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then place a splint according to the size of the limb; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is at the edge of the plantar side of the foot, make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against the broken part of their foot; then wrap it in a long piece of cloth, and place the splint as large as the foot, and hold it in place as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary to place a splint above and another below the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight, then wrap the entire arm around the hand, and bind the injured part between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the other two, if it is the thumb, then make it even as it should be; and strain with the palm, and if you see that it does not move, then place a straight small splint to raise the fractured part, and do not let it move; and if the fracture is in the other two, such as the index or the other, then make it even, and bind with the sound finger that is next to it; or you can tie them all together, as long as it is useful, or place a splint above, as with the thumb; and take care in restoration and positioning of abscess, and protect what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the chest are often broken, and one can see when they turn in front and behind; and the restoration is such that one lies on top of the fractured rib, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the pain is felt above its face, then each of the assistants stretches their line evenly to their part; and it is when the fracture is brought to the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the chest, then one of the lines should be towards the base of the rib, and the other lines away from the fractured rib.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the groin, and then the ligaments above the groin are stretched out, and the extension down; then place the bone even in both hands, as much as possible according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, and do not apply if there is no abscess.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it subside first, then return to your work and care; the bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap it above the fractured part doubled in two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg until the heel comes to the root of the foot, and tie a long thread between the calf and the leg, outside, and bring the upper end of the thread over; then turn back on the leg and on the calf the bandage, then put the splint on the fractured part, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the calf with soft cloth to make it even, then start binding three or four times above the fracture; and the more you go up from the fracture, and the less you strain; then check the two threads that you have tied between the leg and the calf, and the three splints that are above, then return to the top of the thread, until you reach the knee; and the strain, so that it does not move from its place, then let it remain like that, so that there is no abscess or swelling of any kind.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it is dislocated, then remove the joint, and address what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that can be gripped, it should be removed if possible; and if not, then cut the limb, and tear away the flesh; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Never break the ribs in this way, as in the dislocation and shoulder; nevertheless, in the restoration made thus, it does not cause pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And wash the ribs when they are restored at the appropriate times, either a little sooner or a little later, according to the diversities of the conditions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the road of the gentleman
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the road of the gentleman, there is little breakage, but it rains many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is not but a cut, or a puncture, and it has to all wounds, and without wound, and it feels very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts together what is broken to its two parts, as much as it can be assembled, then put on the ointment, and if you have skill, put a round bandage, and hold it as it should be, then reward all the dispositions that we have said in other breakages, such as abscess and similar; and for each accident that it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" on the right side, and the other is called "foscile"; and they break just as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken at once, then the leg returns to its whole state.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, it returns in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, there is great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and it returns outside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, apply gentle traction, make it even, and tie the splints equally; however, if there is a fracture and it is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the traction should be less and lighter; and heal according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that bind the leg on one side and the other, and be long enough to cover the leg from the knee to below; then wrap them around and tie them above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one administers the long cloth of the leg, and it is made of fustian, and properly placed on the break where it has a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; and cure it as soon as it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of bones due to a fall
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but bones due to a fall never break and are only slightly displaced, and there is no injury in most cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones due to a fall, and you see these bones overlying each other, then place the affected limb on the ground, as if it wants to walk, and then put your limb above where the bones are raised, press them so much that they realign; then apply the plaster and bandage, and pour some water onto the plain of the bone, put a small cloth on the wound, then bind the limb evenly, then wrap it with cloths and other things that you know.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the joint is released, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if you restore them as we have said for the two bones of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and it should be slightly wider, then place the cotton tape that I mentioned, and tighten it evenly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and tighten the cotton tape outside the bone; and let it be on top of the head of the splint below the belly of the bone, so that it heals well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other breakages, as we have said; and treat each accident as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone in the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the nature of a woman are broken, if the woman is seated, she should be enlarged, then inclined to the part of the back, and held from behind; then fill the wound of the nature with cotton, and put in as much as I have shown; then lift the woman, and raise the back slowly and slowly, and at that time the cotton will come out through the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, if you remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, then return it, and thus do this for seven days or around: if it will be restored the breakage, and if you see, take a bladder of birds, and tie a catheter to one end, and blow all the bladder into the nature; then blow into the catheter until the bladder is inflated inside: the nature will return the breakage; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in that way for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these broken bones are not hidden from him who puts his study and use to this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means in many positions the right way of restoration: understand therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose feather and blow the thigh; then wrap bandages around, and leave it for three days or enquire around, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has broken with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleansed immediately, so that the cleansings that we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, if the remaining vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the breaker in the same hour, or the next day, if pus does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes, leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the pus is calm, and do not touch it on the next day or the fourth, for you will bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken teeth appear above the gum line, then it is necessary to carefully place them gently in your hands and extend them slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not evenly arranged to be placed in your hands, then use the tool made of iron, which is seven or eight spans long, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this purpose, it should have three or four sharp points, according to the number needed for each treatment of broken bones; and it should be round and a little thick, so that it does not pierce through the member at your work, and it should be sharp in front, and thick in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the patient must have the dislocated shoulder placed on top of the head of the bone; and it is pushed once, as much as it returns, and they are evenly placed one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instruments have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.
