And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then use a suitable instrument, such as a saw or chisel, to your power; then scrape off what remains in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is returned, and the pain is great afterward, do not let it remain in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its natural position, then dress the wound with stiptic black wine, and properly if it has been bruised; and do not put anything on the wound or oil where it might bring about putrefaction and corruption; then administer these remedies as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the dressing all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not compressed with the breakage; many times the foolish man has done this, and has caused the pain or death or corruption at any time; and let the astringents be more mild and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no harmful accident has occurred, as we have said, and you relieve pain to the limb, if it does not require being set; but wrap around, in place of setting, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is discharging pus, remove what you have placed on top of the wound, and put healing ointment on it, such as Tetraflamron and similar ointments.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to move the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be aligned in such a way that the bow can move freely.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to move too much, and it cannot be set back in place, but rather moves like a bow, because of small pieces of bone, then you must first clean the wound with a tent, and remove all those unwanted pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or some other form of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is written in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open in the limb, like the bones of the hip or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not remove it immediately, because often many die, but leave it until it has healed; perhaps it will fall out after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	forcibly applying bandages
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often find after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an unfortunate thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps it cannot do its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, if we find that it is fresh: if you administer stiffening medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acaice, and similar things, so that you do not use any of these things or all together, and mix them with stiffening wine or with plenty of honey or with vinegar; and put it on the nose in a cloth, and hold it well, and do not leave it in the hands for a long time; then loosen it, and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you hold a piece of soft bread well made; because the property of the bread is that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the skin above, and make the superfluousness apparent; or you cut it with any razor until it is removed, and care for it as long as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb that is after the garment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains after the limbs are weak and subtle, there are many causes: one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not reach the members to the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and administer baths, and give joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and the inflammation often of high temperature, until the swelling goes to the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a deformed limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, but does not affect its natural function: thus, one should not believe those who say that one must break the limb entirely in a new way, and many have done this in our land; and such practices are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; however, if the dislocations and twists are recent, it is necessary to apply hot water or softening herbs that have been boiled, such as willow bark, roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things; and the mollifying plaster, such as well-made diaquilon, and you take the willow bark powder, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the plaster on top; or you take figs, and grind them with fennel, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is it necessary to apply continuous and prolonged pressure with wet hands to the dislocation.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the deformity is stiff and hard, like stone, and it needs to be removed with a knife, if it fits over the bone, make a thin incision; and put on bandages and apply treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be returned towards the shoulder.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, the shoulder swells, and if by chance it is reset, it may move to the other side where it is swollen: many times it brings on spasms and other pains; therefore, when this happens, first drain the injury, then leave it until the abscess is calmed; then raise the limb in hot and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is rare that the jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both are according to two methods: either they are slightly bone-hardened from their places, and somewhat softened; or they are completely displaced, and hang down towards the ground, and cover the mouth with saliva so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wrap his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly and not delay; and in such a way that the attendant holds the chief of the painful part against the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand is outside, to hold equal; and commands the patient to soften his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And when the joint is evenly aligned, it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially when both mandibles are involved together, apply hot and oil-soaked cloths until the joints can be gently moved; do not force the resetting as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are evenly aligned and the jaw pain is relieved by softening, apply a cloth made of oiled rose petals and wax, then loosely bandage it with moistened linens; let the patient sleep on their back, with their head between two pillows, so they do not move to the left or right, nor try to open their mouth, but eat light food until the pain is gone, and the jaw is healed; then gradually introduce what they want to eat, and do not force them to open their mouth for eating and drinking until the jaw is completely healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two jaws cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour and are not converted back to their original shape, then there comes fever and sweating as usual, and perhaps diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then cut off that it is a fatal sign; and many times the one who has it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be removed from the side of the body without cutting into it and the surrounding tissue, and it is not reset once dislocated, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the hairs are spread out on their back, and they extend their arms; then press the bone firmly into your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and the bandage, and hold it in place; and the patient who is on the side cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated once, then reset it to its original position, as we have said; then apply the plaster and the bandage, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the same way the patient is brought back from the spasm, when they are freed from their bone.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated: one is that it dislocates at the part of the acromion to the outside; and the second is at the part of the pis; and sometimes dislocates at the part above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocates outwards towards the acromion, especially to those who have little flesh, because to these it is very painful; to those who have enough flesh, it dislocates gently, and returns gently.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some people, percussion or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with an abscess, and thinks it is dislocated by the bone.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must first examine him, until you are certain; and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation is when it is towards the shoulder, and makes a difference between the sick and healthy shoulder, and you will find between their differences manifest; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the shoulder, the top of the shoulder, like if it were two bones; and the bad one cannot put its hand to its neck, nor move from any movements; and also, if it is dislocated above, if it is not hidden, for you will clearly see it at the back; and this way of dislocation is not hidden, when it is new, or if it is infected with bad ones.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the hand of the injured one high, then puts the splints on the outside, and pulls the joint upward to the shoulder; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it high, then puts it down; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said before, then it is necessary that the injured one's hand be bathed in hot water; and the medicine should soften and moisten, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and it should be applied; then the injured one's hand should be laid on their back, and a cloth of equal thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the shoulder, then the injured one's foot should be placed on top of the cloth, and the shoulder is lifted vertically, and the injured one's hand is taken; and other ministers wash the head of the injured one, so that it does not move down; this shoulder has now returned, and if you see that the dislocation is reset according to this manner: and it is that you make sure that the person who is larger than the injured one is standing straight in front of the injured one's side, and bend the shoulder away from the injured one's side, and lift the shoulder up, so that the injured one's hand hangs in the air; and other ministers take the injured one's hand down towards their stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, it can be moved with anything heavy, and the dislocation now returns.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting can also be done in another way: and it is that one places a long, thin rod in the earth, which the patient should hold like a dart, and not too heavy or too heavy; then it is placed away from the pain, but with cloth softly covering, and the pain should be on the long side of the bone; then the hand is extended over the other part firmly, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a rod of two arms and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded for muscles to enter from outside the joint, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie above the chief of the soft cloth, which was not bleached by the pain, then remove it from the side of the pain; and extend one arm over the long, and tie the assistance over the long, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm over the wide edge of a large shield, and extend the hands downwards, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the jointure is now ready.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is ready, in whatever way it is, then you must place a equal woolen ball away from the pain, then apply the poultice with flour from the mill, with incense and a little honey, over the whole shoulder and around, then remove the poultice away from the pain evenly, and return the limb to the poultice, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he massage little, until the limbs are comforted, for it will heal faster; and then massage again after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and it is not made soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is strong due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cautery at three points, as it is placed in front or in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot be raised above the arm, then cut the nerve at the head of the shoulder is torn or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is at the back and the shoulders, or behind, is caused by impulse and extension of the hands, and there is another remedy; and cure until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb becomes swollen and moves slowly, then frequently apply the ointment until the swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and repeatedly dislocates; and it is dislocated from all parts, even in front and behind, and the dislocation has not been repositioned, for one can see and feel it well; and it moves according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the misaligned ear with the healthy one, let the patient see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is sawn off, and it cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as possible, because if it is not reset, it will be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; it is better than other dislocations, but it causes more great pain, and perhaps many die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend your hand to his hands; and his arms are spread, and his hands on either side of the ear, in and out, and push the joint to its place together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and holds the root of the palm of the hand which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the joint, then administer strong extension; and when two people extend the arm, and bind it with two bandages, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from each side, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint at the hand, if there is any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, as much as it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster with some honey on top, and bind it tightly, and put the arm against the back of the shoulder, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, then release the bone and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then restart the bandage and the bone, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly put back; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it hurts after the resetting of the joint and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or place a piece of fat mutton grease on the joint, leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and put in a bath; and when it sweats, rub the joint immediately, then replace the grease, and put in a bath again; and do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see, then place moist warm water with butter on it, and strain it on; and it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than other joints. Therefore, it should be quickly returned to its place at the moment it is dislocated, as long as the limb is swollen or there is an abscess nearby.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is that you place the injured hand on a table, and extend the patient's hand, and the thumb places it evenly so that the palm is over the appearance of the joint, and press it until it returns. Therefore, it is necessary to check if it is properly set; then, place the injured hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's back of their hand on the table, and the practitioner places their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it now returns, that is good; if not, apply calming ointments to the abscess and leave it as such to begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if it cannot be borne, and you cannot place it in position after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and nothing can be done to the patient until the hand is washed, and nothing can be inserted into it: then cut the nerve or artery; otherwise, there is no other means than applying a fire cautery through the skin, and perhaps nothing else is useful.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is dislocated, place the poultice that we have mentioned above, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no inflammation, then use hot vinegar, and rub it until it is healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never dislocate the two fingers at any point, never at the back of the palm or the belly; then hold the two fingers, and strain the dislocation to your palms until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and push it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for three days, and then put it in place that day; and tie it as we have said, and remove the next day, and make it move, and relieve the pain; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healthy; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	back pain from a dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or neck is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, as the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions suddenly rise without volition, and cannot be held, and often all the limbs become soft, or the two hands or the two arms or one, and often the spine moves at four parts; this which moves to the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you reward the gilbositez if it comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or from impacts or similar things, they said in the old ways of cures with great words, but I have abbreviated according to my intention and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of a fracture that comes from the front, there is no engineering or health; and also the one that comes directly to the second rib, and no one can cure except that proper one which comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the hairs should be stretched out over his face in a straight line, and have some strain away from him, so that he does not bleed; then make one bandage at the top on the ground, and the other at the bottom, and tie one ligature outside of the fracture, and the other around the hips, and as the knees, and as the elbows, and as the feet; and two assistants should bind the ligatures, one at the top and the others at the bottom, among the two bandages; and they should be well fastened, the bandage as we have said, and the fingers place their palms on the spine, as long as it regains.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a long board of three arms in length, and bend it away from the pain, and the hairs should be on the side, and push the head of the board away from the pain, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and put the patient's feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the one who turns back to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should fasten two ropes to the head of the dislocated arm, and on the other side of the feet, and between each rope, on both sides, a long palm; and in each rope, there should be a hole, where the turner goes straight, and the ropes should be firmly on the ground, so that they do not move; and between the two ropes, there should be one turning rope, next to the turned limbs, and in the two turns, there should be two small ropes of a long palm, to turn the turner; then tie the middle limb to the head of the turner, and the other limb to the feet of the other turner, and each assistant should turn their turner to the whole limb, and the master should put the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, apply a drying powder with abundant water, then insert a probe, and then place the end of a tablet of three fingerbreadths in length, which impregnates the affected part and the part of the spine with sanity, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle pressure until they are healed; and if anything happens at the end of the healing, then administer medicines that soften and soothe, with the treatment we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never does it appear in the back spine of the back, and one should be careful not to have presumption: by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	That the joints of the hip and shoulder do not come out except as dislocations only, and they are not as other joints; and the joint of the hip is misaligned in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside than that, and slightly misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of misalignment inside is such that when the leg with the bad joint is joined with the good one, it is longer, and more open than the good one, and cannot bend its knee to the fire; and it is the legs that are swollen with abscesses, because the cause of the belly comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who comes after is that this accident is opposite to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of the one who comes before are that he has a well-set leg according to the completion; nevertheless, he does not double over in pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and he retains his urine, and his anger swells, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one who comes after are that he cannot spread his groin, nor double over, and the other leg is more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and the head is dislocated from the neck outside the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The symptoms of this type of dislocation are such that if it is old, and it lasts according to its nature, there is no remedy; and there is no need for it to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, you must return the joint, extend it, and move it to the left and right; perhaps if it returns, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you apply one strong minister, and extend the leg firmly at two hands, or at one hand that is tied above the thigh; and other ministers place their hand under the tail in a similar manner as they bite their fingers off from their toes, then they squeeze it with a soft leather strap around the buttocks; and others grip the head of the limb; and extend up and down all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you should treat its similarity. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary to support the misaligned part on the healthy side of the shoulder, then place the limb at the base of the neck, and the limb that is outside the arm, then extend the limb above the arm, and towards the forceps; then take other ministers to hold the thick limb of the misaligned neck, and extend it in a proper manner: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, it is necessary that you tie the two legs of the dislocated joint together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two ankles, and let the dislocated leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then it should be hung over the top of a stick, and let the arms be stretched out two lengths below the ground; then command the minister to grasp the neck of the chicken, and let another minister hang with the dislocated one, who grasps the neck firmly, for the joint is now healing.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is gone, slice the dislocated joints as we have said in the one with gout, and stretch the rope properly above the dislocated leg and on the foot; then put two knots, one at the head and the other at the foot, then fold the rope between the chicken's legs in the form of a cross; and wrap it with moist cloths around it, so that it does not dry out, then extend each minister towards him, and let the master put the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the flat surface, and press it as we have described in the previous chapter, and cut off the hairs on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the injured leg firmly, and as I have said; and place the fingers of the pain above the angle of the injured limb, then press with the other hand, and extend it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the injured leg downwards, nor to lift it up, but it should be as it was when dislocated to the back, as we have described in the previous chapter; and it should be on its face, and the limb extended as before, and one should press on the joint at the table; and it will be all right when the injured legs are extended, and they are even; then bend the knees, and put the bandage, and the strap of a bandage, so that the back does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release, and put the bandage on; and if you see that they are even, remove the bandage, and let it walk slowly, until the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: namely, internally and externally, and backwards; but it does not dislocate forwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at the hip, and if he cannot do so, it indicates that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is done by making the patient sit upright, and extending his leg as far as possible, and placing your back against his face, and his foot on yours; then take his shoulder in your hands, and bring it between your fingers, and bend the two sides of the shoulder firmly; and other ministers extend his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that he can bend his leg at the hip lightly; and apply the plaster to the leg and hip, and bind them together tightly for three or four hours, then release; and do not work on the patient again until his members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	If the limb is not properly aligned, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the back, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never sprained and never fully dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is dislocated and bent forward to the part where it is dislocated: the remedy is light, and one should gently extend it to their hands when it is sprained only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you should straighten the pain correctly, and hold it with your hands, above the ankle; then pull the bone to yourself with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and strongly strike the bone upwards; do this twice as we have said, pulling and pushing the bone; if it returns, it is good; if not, if you start again, it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, place the pain on its back on the ground, and firmly hold a cloth between its legs, so that the pain does not move; then hold the hands of the ministers to the leg, and other ministers extend the bone to your hands or to the binding, so that they hold the bone while extending it; then extend all the ministers equally, and the cloths should be between the legs of the pain to hold the pain while extending it; then put the equal dislocation in your hands, and other ministers hold the leg clean on the outside, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it reaches the point, if she puts on the plaster and stretches it above, and the bandage forms, and ties the foot to the leg, and warns the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligaments are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligaments break, remove the bandage; then release it on the third or fourth day, and defend against the pain lasting for four days; and if it goes beyond this term, it is certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary to treat it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	For the fire cautery, instruct
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, if they need to be extended, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no way on the back or the knee, it is necessary to make the patient sit with the affected limb straight out or on a table, and place your foot on what opens up from these joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns; and when it is even, and there is no opening, place the sole of your foot on a table at II o'clock for the injured part, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three hours, then release; and let him rest, until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often times the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and you are not knowledgeable in the art and have not used it for a long time, and you are not merciful and slow, and not hard; and at the beginning of things, soothe the inflamed parts, and leave the pain in God’s hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the member immediately, as soon as the inflammation subsides; and when the member is set, then administer soothing remedies, and cure the wound, as it should be, with dry bandages; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are crushed, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and body.
Amen	For the fire cauterization
